Mais en cestui ovraige est paour ou li malaides muert maintenant, ou fistule i vient qui ne puet estre sanee.	But in this work, there is fear that the patient may die immediately, or an ulcer may come which cannot be healed.
de la mice	of the mouse
Quant tu cures la maladie de la mice de ceu que nos avons dit as divisions des cures, et il ne profite mie, adonques i afierent III manieres de cautere que tuit sont boin.	When you treat the disease of the mouse in the ways we have said for the divisions of treatments, and it does not help, then there are three types of cautery that are all good.
Desquelz li une maniere si est que tu faices III cauteres, ou IIII, en lignant selonc la longor de la mice, selonc la figure dou cautere dou foie que nos avons dit devant; et n’apresser mie ta main a tout le cautere, et soit li malaides sovins sor son dos; et une autre maniere de cautere si est que tu eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners, si com nos l’avons mostreit en la dislocation de l’espaule; et lieve le keur qui est endroit la mice, ou li coutes dou malaide vient devers senestre, et soit li elevations dont tu lieves le keur selonc la keur, selonc la longesce dou cors, et li cautere soient selonc la largesce dou cors.	Of which one method is that you make three or four cauteries along the length of the mouse, according to the shape of the liver cautery we have mentioned before; and do not press your hand on the entire cautery, and let the patient lie on his back; another method of cautery is that you heat the cautery which has two prongs, as we have shown in the dislocation of the shoulder; and lift the area where the mouse is located, or where the wound of the patient comes towards the left, and let the elevations with which you lift be according to the direction, according to the length of the body, and the cauteries should be according to the width of the body.
Aprés i boute les II ners enflamez tant que li keurs soit perciez de l’autre part, et puis trai fuers le cautere, et ensi en i avra IIII Et se tu vues, si cauterize a tot le cautere a III ners.	After you put the two nerves aflame until the heart is pierced from the other side, and then draw out the cautery, and thus there will be four. And if you wish, then cauterize all around the cautery for three inches.
Aprés le cure quant il a geteit porriture par lonc tens, et ce vaut mues que li autre des cures devant dites.	After the treatment when it has discharged pus for a long time, and this is worth more than the other treatments previously mentioned.
de ydropisie	of dropsy
Cautere ne vaut a ydropique, fors c’a la maniere qui est apelee «asclytes».	Cautery is not useful for dropsy, except in the method which is called "asclytes.
Quant tu la cures selonc les manieres que nos avons dit en divisions, et ta cure ne profite mie, adonques covient il que tu li faices IIII cauteres entor la boude, et I sus l’estomac, et un sus le foie, et I sus la mice, et II derrier le dos sus l’espinee, et I endroit le pis; et soit li cauteres bien pres de l’espés dou keur.	When you treat it according to the methods we have described in divisions, and your treatment is not beneficial, then you must make four cauteries around the swelling, and one on the stomach, and one on the liver, and one on the spleen, and two behind the back on the spine, and one near the heart; and let the cauteries be close to the area of the heart.
Aprés laisse le cautere aovert por giter porriture lonc tens, et ne lassier mie la cure dou malaide aprés le cautere; et sanation se hasterait, et seront ensamble les II ententions avec l’aide de Deu.	After leave the cautery open to expel pus for a long time, and do not leave the patient's treatment after the cautery; and healing would be hastened, and the two intentions will be together with God’s help.
Li forme dou cautere por le ventre soit li clavile que nos avons devant mostreit; et cil por le dos soit olivaire, selonc ceu qu’il est ci devant mis.	The shape of the cautery for the belly should be the key that we have shown before; and that for the back should be olive-shaped, according to what is placed here before.
de l’enfleure des piez	of the swelling of the legs
Quant li piez sont enflez a celui qui est ydropique, et sont plain d’awe citrine, il covient que tu cauterizes sus le dos dou piet entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire; et lieve ta main avec le cautere sens torner.	When the legs are swollen in one who is dropsical, and they are full of yellow water, you must cauterize on the back of the foot between the little toe and the ring toe; and lift your hand with the cautery without turning.
Et n’entrer mie trop em parfont, ensi sarrait fuers li awe citrine, et soit li cauteres selonc cest forme:	And do not go too deep with the puncture, so as not to break through the yellow bile, and let the cauterization be according to this form:
Aprés fai sus II jambes II cauteres en chescune jambe a la pointe dou cutellaire; et soit li cauteres dou lonc, l’un desoz le genoil devant et l’autre defuers, enmi la jambe; et laisse les cauteres aovers longement sens curer, que li awe en isse; aprés le cure des autres cures que nos avons dit.	After make on both legs two cauterizations in each leg at the point of the kneecap; and let the cauterization be long, one under the knee in front and the other outside, in the middle of the leg; and leave the cauterizations open for a long time without treatment, so that the bile comes out; after treat with the other treatments that we have mentioned.
de la menoison	of the meiosis
Quant solution de ventre vient de froidor et de moistor, tant que li vertus retentive et digestive qui est ou stomac et en l’intestine est afleboie, et ne puet estre curez par manieres de cures; et tu vois le malaide bien soffrant et de fort vertut, si fai I grant cautere sus l’estomac selonc ceu qu’il en a parleit ci devant ou cautere de l’estomac, au cautere circule; et IIII cauteres entor la boude subtilz a tout I cautere clavile subtil, et II cauteres sus les hainches.	When the evacuation of the bowels comes from cold and moisture, such that the retentive and digestive virtues which are in the stomach and intestines are weakened, and cannot be cured by any methods of treatment; and you see the patient suffering greatly but with strong vitality, then make a large cautery on the stomach according to what has been spoken of here before regarding the stomach cautery, the circular cautery; and four small cauterizations around the navel each like a small key cautery, and two cauterizations on the hips.
Et se tu vois les moistors habundans et le malaide soffrant, se li fai cautere sus le poignil, et I cautere sus chaicun yle, et II petis cauteres sus l’estomac delez le grant, car li cure est profitans quant il i a bone aide.	And if you see the moistures abundant and the patient suffering, make a cautery on the wrist, and a cautery on each thigh, and two small cauterizations near the large one on the stomach, for the treatment is beneficial when there is good assistance.
de la cure des emorroydes	of the treatment of hemorrhoids
Quant les emorroydes sont ou fondement, ou une ou plusors, et sont ancienes et sont de grosses humors froides et moistes corrumpues, et sont curees si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie, si fai cauteres: III sus l’espine dou dos, celi qui est tout defuers desoz almecdate poc et poc en triangulant, et I cautere desoz la boude II dois; et se tu penses que ses estomac soit refroidiez, et li viande ne cuise, et on voit enfler la faice, adonques li faice on I grant cautere sus le stomac, si com il est devant dit, et I autre sus le foie, et I autre sus la mice a tout le cautere clavile; et laisse le cautere overt lonc tens.	When the hemorrhoids are in the fundament, one or more, and are old and consist of large cold and moist corrupted humors, and are treated as we have said in divisions, but it does not benefit, then make cauterizations: three on the spine of the back, those which are entirely outside under the almesade, bit by bit in a triangular manner, and one cautery under the buttock two inches; and if you think that his stomach is cooled, and the food does not cook, and swelling of the face is seen, then on the face make one large cautery on the stomach as was previously said, and another on the liver, and another on the spleen with the entire key-shaped cautery; and leave the cautery open for a long time.
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	After treating, heal the place until it is healed.
de la charnositeit qui est nommee «thelul»	of the fleshiness which is called "thelul
Quant tu copes althelul, si eschaufe le cautere qui semble I raseur, et puis le met tout embraseit sus cel althelul copeit; et i laisse tant ta main que li cauteres viegne a la naissance de la voine, de coi li sans cort; fai ceu une fois ou II, et s’il i a mout d’althelul, si cauterize chaicun si com nos avons dit; aprés les cure d’oignemens profitans tant qu’il soient sanez; et se tu cauterizes d’un cautere grant sus alchatim, si avra plus grant aide.	When you cut the althelul, heat the cautery which resembles a razor, and then place it fully ignited on the cut althelul; and leave your hand there until the cautery reaches the base of the vein, from which the blood flows; do this once or twice, and if there is much althelul, cauterize each one as we have said; after that, treat them with beneficial ointments until they are healed; and if you cauterize with a large cautery on the alchatim, it will provide greater aid.
de plaie mal curee	of a wound poorly treated
Quant li malaides ne puet soffrir tailleure ne overture, que nos raconterons en son leu, si vient teil maladie que ne puet estre sanee fuer que par cautere.	When the patient cannot endure surgery or incision, which we will discuss in its place, then comes such a disease that cannot be healed except by cautery.
Quant a aucun vient fistule, et est enveillie et giete porriture et moistors corrumpues, si la doies prover a tot une tente subtil, et garde que tu saiches a tot la tente combien elle a de parfont.	When an ulcer comes to someone, and it is open and discharges pus and corrupted moisture, then you should probe it thoroughly with a fine instrument, and be sure to know the entire extent of its corruption.
Aprés eschaufe le cautere qui semble I raseur, et le boute en la fistule selonc la quantiteit que li tente i est entrée, et rencomence lou cautere tant que cil cors porris et corrumpus soient ars, une fois, ou II ou III, selonc la quantiteit de som besoing; et te warde d’ardre lé nerf qui sunt enqui, et des grans voinnes.	After heat the cautery which resembles a shaver, and insert it into the ulcer according to the depth that the probe has gone in, and repeat the cautery until all the corrupted and putrid flesh is burned, once, or twice or three times, according to the amount needed; and beware of burning the nerves inside, and the large veins.
se li fistule vait au cors de la vesie et a l’intestine, si te warde de ces leus, et ne faire ceu fuers que en leu charnut, et pense qu’ele n’est mie persans; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez, et se li leus est saielez, et les matieres sont ostees lonc tens, adonc saiches que li leus est sanez entierement; et se les matieres ne sont ostees, saiche que li leus est troez, et corrumpus li os au font; et ensi com un de ces que nos dirons en son leu.	If the fistula goes to the body of the bladder and to the intestine, then beware of these places, and do not do this outside of meaty areas, and consider that it is not penetrable; after cure the place until it is healed, and if the wound is stitched up, and the materials are removed for a long time, then know that the wound is completely healed; and if the materials are not removed, know that the wound is deep, and the bone rots at the base; and thus as one of those we will say in its place.
de la maladie des reins	Of the disease of the kidneys
Quant dolor de froit vient as rains, et de grosse ventositeit, et ne prent talant de femme, adonc covient il que tu li fais cautere sus les rains d’une part et d’autre au cautere clavile que nos avons devant dit; et se nos le cauterizons em mileu, si avra III cauteres en ligne, et se feront plus grant aide.	When pain from cold comes to the kidneys, and from great windiness, and he does not desire a woman, then you must make a cautery on the kidneys on one side and the other with the key cautery that we have said before; and if we cauterize in the middle, there will be three cauterizations in a line, and they will provide greater aid.
de la vessie	of the bladder
Quant li vessie est mole et foible de froit et de moistor, si que li malaides retient l’urine, adonc li fai cautere en la partie defuers sus la vessie, la ou encomencent li poil dou poignil, et I a destre et I a senestre, et soit chescuns cauteres si lons com li nous d’un poce; et li fais I cautere defuers le dos, ou II se tu en as besoing; et soit li cauteres clavile selon la forme devant dite.	When the bladder is weak and cold from coldness and moisture, so that the patient holds back urine, then make a cautery on the outer part above the bladder, where the hairs of the wrist begin, both right and left, and let each cautery be as long as the width of one thumb; and also make a cautery outside the back, or two if you need them; and let the cauterizations be key-shaped according to the form previously mentioned.
de la marris	of the marrow
Quant li marrix est froide et moiste, et ne laisse mie por ceu a concevoir, et les flors sont corrumpues et lor termines tarde; et quant elles vienent, si sent grant dolor: adonques covient il c’on li faice III cauteres entor la boude, si com nos avons dit ou cautere de la vessie, et II cauteres defuers le dos; et soit li cauteres clavile, si com nos avons dit.	When the marrow is cold and moist, and does not allow for conception, and the flowers are corrupted and their periods are delayed; and when they come, there is great pain: then it is necessary to make three cauterizations around the navel, as we have said in the cautery of the bladder, and two cauterizations outside the back; and let the cauterizations be key-shaped, as we have said.
de la hainche	of the hip
Quant les moistors viscouses dessendent a la boiste de la hainche, et por ceste cause si se muet de son leu, et li signes est que li cuisse est plus longe que li autre quant on le mesure ensamble; et est trovez li leus dou departement vuis, si covient que tu cauterizes le malaide sus la boiste de la hainche a I cautere semblant au cercle, et seigne devant le leu entor la boiste si com elle torne, si que li boiste soit dedens le cercle; et si soit li cauteres telz com cil dont on a cauterizeit le stomac.	When the viscous moistures descend to the hip joint, and for this reason it moves from its place, the sign is that the thigh is longer than the other when measured together; and the site of the separation is found close by, then you must cauterize the patient on the hip joint with a cautery resembling a circle, and apply it in front of the site around the joint as it turns, so that the joint is inside the circle; and let the cauterization be such as those used to cauterize the stomach.
Et se cist cauteres ne t’est presens, se li fai III cauteres de l’olivaire grans, et soit li cauteres ausi parfont com tous li keurs; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if this cautery is not available to you, make three large cauteries of the olive kind, and let the cautery be as perfect as all the others; and treat it until it is healed.
de la dolor de la hainche	of the pain of the hip
Quant dolor vient en la boiste de la hainche, et c’est de froidor et de moistor, et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en la division et li cure ne vaut, et li maladie est anciene: adonc covient il que tu purges le malaide des grosses humors de pilules fetides, ou autres pilules bones semblans.	When pain comes in the joint of the hip, and it is from cold and moisture, and the patient is treated with what we have said in the division and the treatment does not work, and the disease is old: then you must purge the patient of thick humors with foul pills, or other good pills similar to them.
Aprés li fai cautere; et li maniere dou cautere si est selonc II manieres: c’est a savoir ensamble medicines ardans, et cautere de feu.	After that, apply cautery; and the manner of the cautery is in two ways: namely, with burning medicines together, and fire cautery.
Cautere de feu si est selonc mout de manieres, desquelz li uns est telz: que tu cauterize sus la boiste de la hainche III cauteres triangulalz selonc ceste forme, et i fai bone profunditeit et grant, et ait entre chaicun cautere d’espaice la groissece d’un doi, et soit li cauteres olivaire; aucune fois fait on cautere en mileu sus lou chief de la hainche, por coi il en i a IIII selonc ceste forme:	Fire cautery is of many kinds, one of which is as follows: you apply three triangular cauterizations on the joint of the hip according to this form, and make a good depth and large, and leave between each cautery the space of a thumb's thickness, and let the cauterizations be olive-shaped; sometimes one makes a cautery in the middle on the head of the hip, which is why there are four according to this form:
Et se tu vues, si le cauterize au cautere dou cercle que nos avons devant dit en la dislocation de la hainche; mais fai en teil maniere que li cercles conteigne toute la hainche, et tous li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if you wish, then cauterize it with the circular cautery that we mentioned before in the dislocation of the hip; but do so in such a way that the circle contains all of the hip, and all of the thickness of the joint is burned.
Et c’est li maniere c’on fait en sciatique, quant li dolor tient en la hainche, et ne parvient mie jusc’a la cuisse ne jusc’a la jambe.	And this is the method used for sciatica, when the pain remains in the hip, and does not reach the thigh or the leg.
Et s’ele vient jusc’a la cuisse et la jambe, se li fai II cauteres lai ou li malaides dit que li dolor li tient, et I cautere desus la cheville IIII dois, a la partie senestre un poc; et soit li cauteres cutellaire, et soit arse li espesseté dou keur; et se li malaides sent que li dolor s’estende jusc’a dois dou piet ou pres d’enqui, se le cauterize la ou il sent la dolor III poins ou IIII au cautere qui est apelez «poins».	And if it extends to the thigh and the leg, then make two cauteries where the patient says the pain is held, and one cautery above the ankle four fingers wide, on the left side a bit; and let the cauteries be knife-shaped, and burn through the thickness of the joint; and if the patient feels that the pain extends to the toes of the foot or near them, then cauterize where he feels the pain three points or four with the cautery which is called "points.
Et se mestiers est, se li en fai plus; et se il seit que li dolor soit desoz le genoil vers la cuisse, se li fais cautere au cautere cutellaire ou circulaire, et te done bien garde en tous tes cauteres que tu n’i lassier mie tant le cautere que tu brules les ners et les grans arteres, et que tu ne faices au malaide plus grant nuisance et contraction.	And if needed, I do more for him; and if he knows that the pain is below the knee towards the thigh, I make a cautery with a scalpel or circular cautery, and take good care in all your cauterizations not to leave the cautery so long that you burn the nerves and large arteries, and that you do not cause greater harm and contraction to the patient.
Et je meisme ai veus plusors qui ont fait cautere sus la cheville dou piet, et li lasserent tant que li jambe fut toute enflee, et li piez ausi, et fut perciez et corrumpus toz li piez.	And I myself have seen many who made a cautery on the ankle of the foot, and they left it so long that the leg was entirely swollen, and the foot likewise, and all the foot became perforated and corrupted.
Aprés une solution de ventre dont il ot la mort.	After a purgative from which he received death.
Et se li dolors est en II parties ensamble, fai cautere en l’une et en l’autre, selonc ceste maniere.	And if the pains are in two parts together, make a cautery on one and on the other, according to this manner.
Et li saige dirent en la cautere de la hainche, de coi ci est li maniere, fai I tel fer et soit au chief ausi gros com uns nauvillon de dacte, ou un poc moins, et soit par entrechetres et soit des l’un entrechetres jusc’a l’autre d’espaice la quantiteit d’un nou de poce; et soient li entrechetres aovers de II pars, et soient aussi comme noez, et i ait I mainche de fer bien fait; et c’est li forme:	And the wise men say in the cautery of the hip, this is how it should be done: make such an iron and let it be as thick at the head as a date stone, or a little less, and let it have crossbars and let them be spaced apart by the width of a knuckle from one to another; and let these crossbars be made of two parts, and also like knots, and there should be an iron handle well made; and this is the form:
Et soit eschaufez tant qu’il soit toz rouges et giete senteles, et puis le mette on sus la boiste de la hainche malaide, et soit tornez sus lou sain costeit; et lou cauterize une fois I cautere reont et lou laisse III jors; et puis fai emplaustre de burre, et laisse la plaie aoverte lonc tens; aprés la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	And let it be heated until it is all red and emits sparks, and then place it on the swollen hip of the patient, and turn it towards the healthy side; and cauterize once with a red-hot cautery and leave it for three days; and then make a poultice of butter, and leave the wound open for a long time; afterwards treat with ointment until healed.
Albucasim dit que nos usons poc de cest cautere por la paor de son regart, et se voions poc qui en usent; et toutevoie ceu est des boins cauteres, qui le puet soffrir, et lai ou il s’afiert.	Albucasim says that we use little of this cautery because of the fear of its glance, and we see few who use it; nevertheless, this is one of the good cauteries, which can be endured by those to whom it is suitable.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant si est que tu faices I estrument a entrechetres en coi dessende li marge de la porte, et soit d’arain ou de fer a une paroit longe, et en la hautece ait II nous, et ait entre chaicun la quantiteit de la groissece d’un doi; et soient overt defuer et desus, et se joignent ensamble selonc ceste forme:	The cautery of burning medicine is such that you make the instrument to interlock in which descends the margin of the door, and it should be made of bronze or iron with one side long, and in height have two inches, and between each have the quantity of the thickness of a thumb; and they are open below and above, and join together according to this form:
Aprés met sus la boiste de la hainche au malaide gisant sor suin costeit sain, et apresse ta main mout sus la boiste de la hainche; aprés giete entre les II cercles de l’awe chaude qui soit chaufee au feu I poc, et li laisse une houre dou tens, et soffre li malaides la chalor et l’arsure de li.	After place on the hip joint of the patient lying on their healthy side, and press your hand strongly on the hip joint; then pour between the two circles of the hot water which has been heated over fire one cup, and leave it for one hour in time, and let the patient endure the heat and burning from it.
Car il i trueve mordication ausi com de feu; et quant li mordications iert passee, se lieve ta main avec l’estrument et leve la hainche d’awe douce, et laisse ensi III jors, et met sus burre tant que ceu qui est noir de l’eschaudure soit osteit; et lou laisse III jors que porriture en istrait; et ceu serait li derriene aide aprés le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	For there is a burning sensation as if from fire; and when the burning has passed, raise your hand with the instrument and lift the hip with warm water, and leave it this way for three days, and apply butter until what is blackened by the scalding is removed; and you leave it for three days so that pus may come out; and this would be the final aid after treating with ointments until it is healed.
Et se li dolor s’est estendue jusc’a la cuisse ou jusc’a la jambe, se li fai I estrument que teigne awe selonc ceu que tu as fait en la hainche igaument; et c’est li maniere de l’awe chaude, et je l’ai escripte ou traitier de la rectification de medicine.	And if the pain has spread to the thigh or to the leg, make an instrument that steeps in warm water according to what you have done for the hip equally; and this is the method of warm water, and I have written it in the treatise on the correction of medicine.
Pren alcali et chaulz vive, autant de l’une com de l’autre, et les broie ensamble, et les met en I nuef pot.	Take alkaline and quicklime, an equal amount of each, and grind them together, and put them in a new pot.
ou il ait I petit pertuis defuer se que li pointe d’un raisor i puisse entreir; et met desor celui pot I autre pot bien plombeit, et met sus alcali et chalz et awe douce sus, tant qu’il en i ait I doi desus les poudres cant tu l’avras bien preingte a ta main; et le laisse ensi tant qu’il en dessende awe ague et chiece ou pot plombeit, puis pren toute cele awe, et la giete sus chalz et sus alcali si com devant.	where there is a small opening to blow so that the tip of a razor can enter; and put over that pot another pot well sealed, and add alkali and heat and soft water on top, until there is two fingers above the powders when you have taken them well in your hand; and leave it thus until the water descends and falls into the sealed pot, then take all that water, and throw it over heat and alkali as before.
Et lors si sera mout ague et est aministree en mou d’ovraiges de medicine et en cauteres d’autres membres Car elle fait auteil oevre com feus, et si a autres medicines dont on cauterize bien la hainche ensi com tesisie et miel anacardi et chalz avec savon, toutes ces choses mellees ensamble.	And then it will be very watery and is administered in many works of medicine and in cauteries of other members; for it does the work of fire, and it has other medicines with which one cauterizes the hip as well as resin and anacardi and heat with soap, all these things mixed together.
Et Galiens nos raconte une cure dont uns hons fut curez de la dolor de la hainche et de la voine sciatique, et lou loe mout, et dit que on n’i fist autre cure, et qu’il en fut sanez a une soule fois quant on ot fait ceste cure, et il se fut baigniez si com il l’enseigne ci aprés.	And Galien tells us of a treatment where a man was cured of the pain in his hip and sciatic nerve, and he praises it greatly, and says that no other treatment was done, and that he was healed in one single time when this treatment was performed, and he bathed as he instructs hereafter.
Et dist en teil maniere que tu preignes dou litargire vert fres et sec, et le broie mout avec I poc de graisse, et met sus la hainche et sus la cuisse et sus la jambe ou la dolor tient, et la lie; et li laisse III houres et par la quantiteit que li malaides ne sente plus l’arsure.	And he says in such a manner that you take green vitriol fresh and dry, and grind it well with pork fat, and put it on the hip and thigh and leg where the pain is, and apply it; and leave it for three hours until the patient no longer feels the burning.
Et puis le fai entrer ou bain tant que li cors li soit un poc arousez, et lou fai entrer ou lit, et li dolor s’en ira toute et sera sanez.	And then make him enter the bath until his body is a bit warmed, and make him enter the bed, and the pain will go away entirely and he will be healed.
Et saiches que nuls ne doit user de cautere de telz medicines, se ceu n’est aprés l’evacuation de cors.	And know that no one should use such cauterization or medicines, if not after the evacuation of the body.
Et Dyascorides dist que quant li voine sciatique est cauterizee de fiens de chievre, si i aide mout; et doit estre fais li cauteres en teil maniere.	And Dioscorides says that when the sciatic vein is cauterized with goat's fat, it helps greatly; and the cauterizations should be done in such a manner.
Prenez lainne et la beurez d’oile vielz, et metez sus la fossete qui est entre le pouce dou piez et l’autre qui est apelez foscile.	Take wool and anoint it with old oil, and place it on the indentation that is between the big toe and the other one which is called the instep.
Aprés pren fiens de chievre sec, et l’empren a feu tant qu’il soit charbons, et lou met sus la laine, et le laisse tant qu’il soit estains; et refai encor ensi, et ne cesser de faire ensi tant que tu penses par sens qu’il viegne jusc’a la hainche, et que li dolor soit cessee; et cist manieres de cautere est apelez «cautere de chievre».	After take dried goat's fat, and press it to fire until it becomes charcoal, and put it on the wool, and leave it until it is burned; and do again in this way, and do not stop doing so until you think by sense that it reaches the hip, and the pain ceases; and this manner of cauterization is called "goat's cauterization.
de la dolor dou dos	of the pain of the back
Quant dolor vient au dos, ou par cheoir ou de percussion ou par trop grant evacuation, ou par semblans de matiere espandue froide, a nule de ces semblances ne vaut cauteres, fuer que a celi qui vient de infusion de froide matiere.	When pain comes to the back, whether by falling or by percussion or by too great an evacuation, or by similar cold matter spread out, none of these appearances is suitable for cauterization, because it comes from the infusion of cold matter.
Il covient c’aprés ceu que li malaides est voidiez de pilules fetides ou d’autres semblans, que on li faice sus lou dos, lai ou li dolor tient, trois lignes signies d’enche, et en chescune ligne V cauteres ou plus selonc la vertut et la quantiteit que li malaides puet soffrir; et soit fait li cauteres selonc le cautere qui est apelez «poins»; et se tu vues, fai III cauteres ou IIII au cautere clavile moien selonc ceste forme:	It is necessary after the patient has been purged of foul pills or other similar things, that on his back where the pain persists, three lines are marked out, and in each line five cauterizations or more according to the strength and quantity that the patient can endure; and let the cautery be done according to the cautery which is called "point"; and if you wish, make three or four cauteries with a medium-sized claw cautery according to this form:
Maintes fois vient ceste maladie as petis enfans, et li signes de l’encomencement si est qu’il ont estroite alainne quant il se lievent, et paor; et tu trueves en la derriene espinee dou dos et en nous l’apparance qui vient sus les autres espinees.	This disease often comes to small children, and the signs of the beginning are that they have a tight abdomen when they wake up, and fear; and you find on the last spine of the back and in us the appearance that comes over the other spines.
Quant tu vois ceu et tu le vues curer, si le cauterize au cautere de celcle selonc ceste forme.	When you see this and wish to cure it, then cauterize it with the circular cautery according to this form.
Si que li cautere porpreigne chescune partie de l’espinee egaument.	So that the cautery marks each part of the spine equally.
Et se tu vues, si cauterize entor l’espinee au cautere poignant II lignes ou III, et soient li poins pres l’uns de l’autre.	And if you wish, then cauterize around the spine with a sharp cautery two lines or three, and let the points be close to each other.
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez selonc ceu que nos avons dit, et warde que tu n’amenistrer cautere en gilbositeit qui soit en spame de nerf.	Afterwards, treat the area until it is healed according to what we have said, and beware that you do not apply cautery to a swelling that is in spasm of a nerve.
de la dolor des jointes	of the pain of the joints
Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere: fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	When the pain of joints is from moisture that spreads to each member of the body, and when the pain comes in feet, which the doctor calls "gout" properly, and when it is of cold cause and treatments of medicines cannot cure it, then it is cured by cauteries in such manner: make many cauteries around the joint of the foot, and let the cauteries be olive-shaped according to this form:
Et s’il i a besoigne que tu poignes sus la faice dou piet, se li fai cautere a tot le cautere c’on claime «point».	And if there is need that you press on the sole of the foot, then make a cautery over the entire area called "point".
Et se les dolors viegnent jusc’a genous et as autres jointures, et ceu avient maintes fois, se li fai cautere sus chaicun genoil III cauteres ou IIII de chescunne partie, a tout le cautere olivaire; et se tu as mestier de plus, si en fai plus, mais n’i tenir mie ta main fuers que tant que li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if the pains come down to the knees and other joints, which often happens, make a cautery on each knee three or four in each part, all olive-shaped; and if you need more, then make more, but do not hold your hand so long that the thickness of the skin is burned.
Et se les dolors dessendent jusc’a genoil et au dos, se li aministre le cautere que nos avons dit en son chapistre.	And if the pains descend to the knees and the back, then administer the cautery that we have mentioned in its chapter.
Et se les dolors sunt as mains, si fai poins entor le foscile II lignes; et s’il remaint point de dolor as dois, si fai poins sus chescune jointe et sus lou poil de la main; et se les dolors vienent jusc’as coutes ou jusc’as espaules, si cauterize chescune partie, et fai boin governement au malaide et penre medicines.	And if the pains are in the hands, make points around the palm two lines; and if there remains any pain in the fingers, make points on each joint and on the hair of the hand; and if the pains come to the elbows or to the shoulders, cauterize each part, and give good care to the patient and proper medicines.
Car se tu li fais boin governement et tu purges fleume, si sera saneis a l’aide de Deu.	For if you give him good care and you purge phlegm, he will be healed by the grace of God.
de la routure dou syfac	Of the treatment of dysphagia
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor; et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre; aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors; puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When rupture comes in the groin, and the testicles descend to the thighs and this is new, then it is necessary that when you wish to treat him, he does not eat on that day; and he uses things that loosen the belly, so that the bile descends from his stomach; afterwards make him sit upon his back between your hands, and command him to strain his groin until the testicles are repaired, and hold them with your hands, and anoint below the rupture on the bone of the thigh, and do a sign that is similar to half a circle above the body; then heat the cautery which here is its form:
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles.	until it is white and it gives off sparks.
Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu; et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu’il ne retornent arrier; et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui I cussin et I serjant sus les cuisses, et I autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains; puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l’os, et se tu ne l’ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere; que tu ne le brulasses; et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz.	Then hold the testicles in their place; and the assistant should press his hand so they do not return backward; and massage well the thighs of the patient, and put a cushion under him and one bandage on the thighs, and another on the chest which holds the hands; then apply the cautery to the sign with your whole hand, and hold it straight and keep it until you reach the bone, and if you do not reach it the first time, repeat again until you come to the bone; and carefully ensure that the testicles do not escape when you are making the cautery; so as not to burn them; and by this means the patient does not die or suffer other harms.
Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien.	And know that when you do not reach the bone with the cautery, your work is worth nothing.
Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d’ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure; aprés III jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’autres oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez, et gise li malaides XL jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee; et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d’aler en chambres.	And the cautery for children must be fine according to their size, and for adults it should be larger according to their measure; after three days clean the area of the cautery with butter until the burn is removed; afterwards treat it with other ointments until it heals, and the patient lies forty days on their back until the wound is well sealed; and their nourishment must be restricted for a long time so that the scab does not rise when they begin to move about in rooms.
Et aprés XL jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse XL autres jors; et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire; et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement.	And after forty days, when he wishes to rise, let a well-made bandage be applied, and wear it for another forty days; and have good rest, work little, and beware of too much drinking and eating, and of shouting too loudly; and when he follows this instruction, he is entirely healed.
Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	And I will say hereafter the treatment of cutting in his chapter.
de la routure dou ventre	of the rupture of the abdomen
Quant routures vienent en autres ventres et sont connisans, et tu vues qu’elles ne croissent plus, se li fai I cautere dou cautere reont selonc sa quantiteit, et soit ars li tiers dou keur; aprés le cure selonc ceu que nos avons dit; et aucun des anciens ont dit c’on le doit cauterizer au cautere a III angles selonc ceste forme:	When ruptures occur in other abdomens and are known, and you see that they do not grow anymore, if the fire cautery is to be applied according to its quantity, let one-third of it be burned; afterwards treat according to what we have said; and some of the ancients have said that it should be cauterized with a three-angled cautery according to this form:
mais signe premier le leu d’enche et fai une ligne per la largesce desus la routure, et une autre defuers, et main ta main emmi a tout le cautere clavile.	but first mark the place to be treated and make a line across the width above the rupture, and another outside, and hold your hand in the middle of the whole key-shaped cautery.
Mais li premiers cauteres est plus legiers et muedres.	But the first cauterization is lighter and gentler.
de dolor anciene en aucun membre	of old pain in any limb
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor.	When pain comes in any limb, whether from falling or striking, and that pain lasts a long time, and the cure of medicine does not work, then it is necessary to cauterize it with the cautery which is called «point», and let the cauterization be according to the length of the limb and its smallness and its weakness and its virtue and its location for twisting and its pain.
s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien; se ceu nom, recomence I autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	If it is healed by the first cauterization, that is good; if not, begin another cauterization on that area, for such is the custom that it should be changed to a part of the limb that is closer, which is why you must perform the cauteries until the patient is healed.
de meselerie	of mixing
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie.	The mixed ailments are sometimes cured by cautery with great help, and especially the diseases that come from the putrefaction of phlegm and melancholy.
Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai V cauteres sus lou chief: I emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous; et II sus les II cornes, et I derrierre sus le haiterel; et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir; et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	When you see it needs to be cauterized, beware if the disease is in its beginning stage, and if it is treated according to what we have said in the division, and does not subside or remain, and you fear that the corruption may spread throughout the patient, then make V cauteries on the head: one in the middle of the head at nine, another towards the forehead at the end of the hair; two on both temples, and one behind on the nape; and leave your hand there until the cauterization reaches the bone, and until the scabs come out so that the vapors from the thick humors can escape; and cauterize it on the mouse as described before.
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse; et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et I cautere en som lou neis, et II cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et VI cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et I grant sus la crupie et I autre delez, et II sus les II espaules; et II sus les coutes, et II sus les tendrons dou pis, et I sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains; et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler; et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et I autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et I autre sus lou foie.	And if the infection is spread everywhere; and it shows clearly, then you must cauterize it with those cauters we have mentioned at the top, and one cautery on the neck, and two cauters on the spine of the neck, and six cauters on the spine of the back, and one large one on the rump and another nearby, and two on the two shoulders; and two on the ribs, and two on the tendons of the breast, and one on each joint of the hands and feet, and on the hollows of the hands; and beware of the nerves that are on the rear heel, so you do not burn them; and sometimes one does cautery on the bone of the wrist, and another on the bone of the stomach, and another on the liver.
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite; et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus.	And know that the more cautery I do, the more help I give, and it benefits him; and know that the patient does not feel pain from the cautery as the healthy person would feel, because the body is already entirely corrupted.
Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers.	And it is necessary that the cauteries be large and small according to the members and joints, according to what you will find in methods of irons.
Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	After treatment, apply the place with flour of violets and honey and other treatments until it is healed.
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre; et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	When swelling comes in any limb and is treated with medicines, oils, and plasters, and it is not healed, then make cauteries on the limb according to its size and smallness; and let the cautery slightly penetrate into the thickness of the skin; then treat it with ointments until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure; et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	And sometimes a cautery is made on the hand and foot and back, at the outlet of the nerve that moves the limb, and thus the swelling is removed; and nevertheless, no one should intervene unless they are knowledgeable about the limbs and the outlets of the moving nerves of the body.
de albaras	of arthritis
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color; puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie; et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the disease which is called "arthritis" is awakened, and medical remedies are of no use, then cauterize it with a hot iron according to the quantity of the thickness of the skin until the whitening is removed, and its color changes; then treat it with flour of vetches and lentils with rose oil and plantain leaves, and blood of pigeon and blood of turtle dove, of each one part; and mix all together, and bind it with a cloth, and apply it to the place until it heals.
li cure de chancre par cautere	the treatment of chancre by cautery
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble I cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.	When chancre comes at the beginning, and you want to stop it, then cauterize it with an iron that resembles a circle, all around the edge of the chancre.
Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre; et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois; et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	And nevertheless the wise say that one should make a cautery in the middle of the ulcer; and yet this does not seem good to me, for I fear it may become ulcerated and corrupted, and I have seen it happen sometimes; and a more straightforward thing is that it be cauterized around, with the cautery which is called "circle", as we have said much about cauteries.
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	of the swelling that cannot die
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens; et tu la vues haster de meurer: adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant; aprés le laisse ensi.	When someone has a disease that is called "adubelati", and it lingers without dying either because of the excess it produces or due to the age of the patient when they are decrepit (that is, too old) and have little blood, or because of the season; and you want to hasten its death: then cauterize around with many small cauteries slightly; afterwards leave it thus.
Car elle se hastera de meureir.	For she will hasten to heal.
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you wish to pierce it with the entire cautery, then heat the cautery in this manner which is its form:
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis.	And place your hand in the middle of that disease which is called "adubelati" until the cautery has pierced the heart, and let the cautery be such that the patient feels it externally in such a manner that the course of the putrefaction is alleviated.
Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	After the treatment until he is perfectly healed.
li cure dou feu par fer	the fire treatment by iron
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches.	Another kind of disease there is which is called "corrodens," and it is nothing other than a consumption of the limb, for it consumes the limbs as fire consumes dry wood.
Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est; aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit.	If you see this disease in a place that can endure cautery with fire together, then heat the clavile cauterizing tools both small and large, according to what is suitable for the place where the disease is; afterwards cauterize all around until you reach all the corruption, and none of it remains, so that everything which is corrupted be removed.
Et puis le laisse III jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption.	And then leave it for three days, and put on the cauterized areas burnt plaster mixed with oil until the burns from the fire are removed, and all the corruption.
Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.	Afterwards apply ointments that promote flesh growth.
Et se tu vois aprés III jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus.	And if you see after three days that healthy flesh does not grow, it is good; and if not, then repeat the cautery on what remains of the corrupted areas.
Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu; mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division: pren la quant tu en as mestier.	And this treatment is sometimes cured by medicinal herbs in place of fire cautery; but still fire cautery is of greater help, and I have already said the cure of the medicinal herbs in the section: take it according to what you need.
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	of the hemorrhoids that come to the feet
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet.	Often it happens that on the feet outwardly grows a disease which is called "clos" according to our intention, and it is a large swollen thing that hurts the foot.
Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc II manieres.	And the cauterization of this disease is according to two methods.
C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude.	That is to say, fire cauterization, and hot water cauterization.
Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe I cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges; aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou; et lou laisse ensi III jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture; puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines.	Fire cautery is such that you heat the cautery to a point as fine as a goose feather, and it should be made of good iron to the size that it can surround the nail on all sides, and that there are subtle edges; after which you place it completely hot upon the nail, and turn your hand entirely around the nail until it reaches the base of the nail; and leave it thus for three days until it begins to emit pus; then apply a poultice of ground wild mallows mixed with tar, and leave the poultice on throughout the night, and the nail will fall out and be uprooted from its roots.
Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then clean the ointment site scraping flesh until it is healed.
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude; et est en teil maniere: pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues; et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine; et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre; puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines.	And if they are turned outward on the body, and this often happens in hands and feet, then you must apply a cautery of hot water; it is done in this manner: take a cane of boxwood or iron, or a goose feather, and place it over the nail and the corns, that is to say warts; and put the cane so that it surrounds everything, then pour some hot water on it, and hold your hand well, and press your hand while turning so that the edge of the cane reaches the root of the nail, and allows the hot water to penetrate deeply down to the root; and let the patient endure a bit of the burning sensation of the hot water for an hour; then leave it this way, and it will be uprooted completely from its roots.
Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	Thus do one after another until you strengthen all those that are of the body, then treat them with ointments that generate flesh.
li cure dou trembler	cure the trembling
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices IIII cauteres ou IV sus l’espinee dou dos, I cautere entre chescune espinee; et I cautere ou pez, et I sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire; si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	When someone trembles from cold, nerves, or quartan fever or another, it is necessary that you make four cauteries or four on the spine of the back, one cautery between each vertebra; and one cautery on the foot, and one on the stomach with an olive-shaped cautery; it will stop the trembling, and hasten the health from the cold disease.
des pustules puans	of smelly pus-filled boils
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues.	Sometimes there appear on the surface of the body blisters or smelly pus-filled boils that come from corrupted large materials.
si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule: un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire.	so it is necessary at first when they appear to make a cautery on each head of the pustule: a subtle cautery of myrtle wood, of which the point should be grasped by fire, or of long birthwort root, or of the lentil-shaped cautery.
Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez; mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	And sometimes they are cauterized at the beginning when they appear, according to this method, and they cannot grow any further, but the excess from which they come is broken, and they are healed; but it must be done after the evacuation of blood.
quant li artere est copee	when the artery is cut
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses; et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	Many times there are great flows of blood from the artery that is cut at the wound that comes to the surface, or in the incision of an abscess, or in the cautery of the limb, and in similar things; and it is a very difficult thing to stop.
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus; puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge; puis empren I, ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	And nevertheless when this happens to anyone, you hasten to place your index finger upon the wound of the vein, and hold it tightly until the blood is calmed beneath your finger, and no drop comes out; then put in the fire the olive cauteries, both small and large, until they are all red; then take one, whether large or small according to the wound and the place where the artery lies, and put the cautery upon that vein where you hold your finger, and keep the cautery upon it until the blood is restrained.
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement I autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	And if it jumps out when you lift your finger from the vein, and the cautery is extinguished, then take hastily another of the cauters that are in the fire.
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez; et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide; et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des IIII manieres que nos avons dit: ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc; et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	And do not cease to do this one after the other until the blood is stopped; and beware that you do not burn the nerve that is nearby, and that no other harm comes upon the patient; and know that when blood flows from an artery, it cannot be easily restrained unless by one of the four ways we have mentioned: either by cautery, or by extraction when it is not treated, or by tightly binding with thread, or by applying medicines that have the power to stop blood; and let it be tied and bound appropriately.
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	Who administers the treatment of tightly binding with cloths or placing burning things upon it, or other similar things, does not profit if the pus is not present.
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne; et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez; et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	And if this happens to anyone and there is no physician or medicine present, he must place his index finger on the vein wound as we have said, and stretch well until it is constricted over the wound and the vein; and he should not move it but anoint it with very cold water often so that the blood is frozen and thickened and constricted; and do this before using cautery and medicines.
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	Here begins the second book of the cures for wounds.
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres; et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	We have told you in the first chapter about all diseases where fire cautery or burning medicine is needed, and the indications and causes and materials and forms of the cauteries; and I have placed that chapter from head to foot, and I will go by the same way in this chapter so that one can find more easily what they want.
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	And before I begin this, it is necessary, dear son, that you learn that in this chapter there is more danger and fear than in the first of cauterizations, and for that reason greater caution is needed.
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses; ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	For in the work of this chapter, there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie.	And I admonish you that you do not undertake folly.
Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures.	For many kinds of people come for treatment.
si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice; et de ces doit on avoir paor.	such come from those who were so afflicted by their illness that they changed quickly due to the madness they found in their illness, and the severity of its malice; and of these one must have fear.
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit: «atendez, je sui garis»; et li maladie est despitouse.	And among these there are who regain their senses and say: "wait, I am cured"; and the illness is spiteful.
Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los; et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie; et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	It is not fitting that you consent to those who come to you with this manner, but place greater trust in your honor than in your desire, and do not open up foolishly but wisely about what you are certain of, and from which you can gain praise; and use prognosis and indication in the treatment of your patients to whom salvation is converted; and this will help you achieve good reputation, and glory, and lasting praise.
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	Very dear son, May our Lord grant you good understanding and righteousness, and if he wishes to inspire you with the holy inspiration of his hand, amen.
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	Or I have ordered this chapter by dividing it into sections, according to what is before in the chapter of cauterizations, that I have divided from head to foot, so that you find more easily what you will need.
dou chief plein d’aigue	from the head full of water
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant; et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	Know that this disease often comes to children at birth, and when it is given too strong a pull on the child's head; and sometimes it comes from an unknown cause.
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors; et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	And I have never seen this disease except in children, and in all those I have seen the death was swift; and for that reason it seems to me not worth laboring over such cases.
Et je vis I enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir; et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os; et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large; et soit ausi longe com II nous, tant que li mostor corre; et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	And I saw a child whose head was filled with water, and the head swelled each day until it could not be supported; and the moisture grew so much that it caused death, and this moisture gathers under the bone on the siphon, between the skin and the bone; and the work is such when the moisture is between the skin and the bone, and the abscess is small, that you cut through the head a wide slit; and let it be as long as two fingers, until the moisture flows out; and see here the form of the spatumile.
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai II fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	If the moisture is thicker, and the abscess is larger, make two incisions in the shape of a cross, according to this form:
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut: si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief III fendures selonc ceste maniere:	And if the moisture is under the bone, and the signs you see are the openings of the head spread on each side, and the liquid squirts out forcefully when you press it with your hand from inside, and this does not return to you: then you must make three incisions in the middle of the head according to this manner:
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers.	And after the incision, extract all the moisture out.
Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor; puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	After extracting the incisions with cloths and powders, and put wine and oil in them, and leave it this way until the fifth day; then untie it, and treat the wound with bandages and ointments, and continue to bind the head evenly, and give the patient dry food with little moisture until the limb is strengthened and healed.
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue; car aucune fois est elle devant; aucune fois derrier; aucune fois en destre; et aucune fois en senestre.	And another method of incision is that you look where the swelling of the abscess opens, and where the accumulation of the fluid gathers; for sometimes it is in front; sometimes behind; sometimes on the right; and sometimes on the left.
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir; et warde que tu ne coper l’artere; et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	Cut then there where the abscess opens, and the accumulation of the fluid, and make an incision according to what you are able; and beware that you do not cut the artery; and if blood flows out, the patient may die from the loss of blood and the evacuation of moisture.
de reume	of gout
Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les II arteres.	When it happens that someone has a disease called "catarrh" in the eyes or nose, and the illness is old, and the medical treatment does not help, then the final remedy is cauterization along with cutting the two arteries.
Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief; aprés li frotte lou leu d’un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout I drapel; puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l’une et de l’autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues; puis signe les leus d’enche, puis cope l’une et l’autre d’un spatumile agut de II pars, tant que li taille veigne jusc’a l’os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief.	So when you cut the veins, the patient must tilt his head back; then rub the area with a rough cloth until the arteries appear, then have the patient compress his neck to all the cloth; then look where the vein lies, and the areas of both are behind the ears, and they are placed close together; then mark the points to cut, then cut each with a sharp two-edged scalpel until the cut reaches the bone, and this should be through the width of the head.
Et se tu vues, boute le spatumile desoz l’artere et la cope au desus, en taillant ausi com II dois au traver.	And if you want, place the scalpel below the artery and cut above it, slicing also as two times across.
Et quant li voinne est copee, si saut li sans en haut continuelment fuers.	And when the vein is cut, the blood jumps up continuously outward.
Et se li artere n’apert au sentir, si covient que tu mesures la quantiteit de l’espaice de III dois, puis seigne d’enche et fent jusc’a l’os; et ceu qu’il covient dou sanc mettre fuers si est VI c/, et par aventure un poc plus ou moins, selonc ce que li malaides puet soffrir, et la repletion de l’artere; puis regarde la plaie: s’il remaint sus l’os point dou syphac, si le cope que apostemes chaus n’i veigne, puis estrain la plaie et lie, et la cure d’oignement tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And if the artery does not open to the touch, then you must measure the quantity of space by three fingers, then incise and cut until the bone; and what is necessary of the blood to be put out is six ounces, and perhaps a little more or less according to what the patient can endure, and the repletion of the artery; then look at the wound: if it remains on the bone some of the syphac, cut so that hot abscesses do not come, then drain the wound and tie it, and the treatment with ointment until it is healed.
de emigrainne	The term "emigrainne" does not appear to be standard in any known medieval medical text or in modern medical terminology. It seems possible that this could be a misspelling or an archaic form of a word related to migraines, which are severe headaches. If we assume it is meant to refer to migraines, then "de emigrainne" might loosely translate to something like "about migraines" or "concerning migraines." However, without more context, providing an exact translation or meaning is challenging.
Quant emigrainne anciaine vient, et catarre agut, por les moistors des larmes et les chalors en temples et sode anciene forsenee et semblans choses, et il est medicinez par manieres de cures de medicine et tout ceu ne li profite mie, si estraions les arteres des temples et lou cauterizons, si com nos avons conteit.	When old emigrainne and acute catarrh come from the moisture of tears and heat in the temples and old sode forsenee and similar things, and it is treated by methods of medical cures and all that does not help him, then we extract the arteries of the temples and cauterize them, as we have recounted.
Et li maniere de l’estraction d’elles si est que li malaides faice rere les poilz de ses temples, et entende a l’artere qui apert en la temple, car elle apert bien par son batement, et est poc reponue fuers que en aucuns homes qui sont trop froit; et s’elle est reponue, si estraigne son col li malaides d’aucuns drapelz, puis frote le leu d’aucun aspre drap, et arose le leu d’aigue chaude tant que li artere apere manifestement; puis pren le spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	And the method of extracting them is that the patient should pull back the hairs on his temples and focus on the artery that appears in the temple, for it shows clearly by its pulsation, and is sometimes more hidden than in some people who are too cold; and if it is hidden, then the patient should tighten the neck with some cloths, then rub the area with a rough cloth, and pour warm water over the area until the artery appears clearly; then take the spatumile of which this is the form:
puis escorche le cuir legierement tant que tu veignes a l’artere, puis la trai en haut as pinceures, et la depart bien des toiles que sont desoz li de chescune partie; et se li artere est subtilz, si la torne a la pointe de l’uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantiteit des II chiés.	Then scrape the skin lightly until you reach the artery, then pull it up to the pinchers, and separate it well from the tissues that are beneath on each side; and if the artery is thin, then turn it with the point of the hook, then cut it from that part according to the quantity of two shoulders.
Car s’elle n’est copee, si ne saut mie li sans dou tout en tout.	For if it is not cut, then the sinew does not jump completely altogether.
Et trai dou sanc des VI c/, jusc’a III; et se li artere est grans, si covient que tu la lies en II leus d’un fil double fort de soie, que porriture n’i veigne devant le soudement de la plaie, et veigne decorremens de sanc; puis cope la superfluiteit qui est entre les II liiens en celle houre meisme, et puis, se tu vues, si lou cauterize dou cautere cutellaire jusc’a l’os tant que li chiés soient copez; et c’est li muedre oevre, se li malaides n’a fievre et il est de chaude complexion.	And let the blood drain for six ounces, up to three; and if the artery is large, then it must be tied in two places with a strong double silk thread, so that putrefaction does not come before the healing of the wound, and bleeding continues; then cut off the excess between the two ties at that same hour, and then, if you wish, cauterize it with the knife cautery up to the bone until the joints are cut; and this is the most difficult work, if the patient does not have a fever and is of a hot temperament.
Car li cauteres est aide por finir les moistors: por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors.	For the cautery is helpful to end the moistures: for this reason it is of greater help against moistures.
Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites; et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez; et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient; et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de II pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	For the extraction of arteries, it is necessary that one fill the place with old cotton and put well-made bandages on top; and when they are untied, apply dry medicines that promote flesh growth and more bandages until it heals; and if bleeding from the artery continues as you work there, hurry to cut by cautery, or use vitriol in the area and press it with your hand to stop the bleeding; and if you do not have this available, place something on the spot so that the blood is congealed, and rinse the area with cold water until the bleeding stops, and apply pressure as needed; and what is more effective and lighter for extracting an artery is to cauterize the vein with a cutting cautery of two parts, but make sure the cuts are well thick to maintain their heat longer.
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	For when the instruments are too weak, they hold less of their heat.
Et doit avoir entre les II coutelz I doit de gros d’espaice, et puis quant tu as signiet d’enche les II leus, et tu mes lou fer ardant sus tant qu’il viegne jusc’a l’os, et cope la voinne en II leus; et soient esloigniet entre les II chiés car il n’est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And there must be between the two knives one thickness of space, and then when you have marked where to join the two places, and you place the burning iron on until it reaches the bone, and cut the vein in two places; and they should be apart between the two shoulders because it is not entirely sealed by this cautery; and this is the form of the cautery:
des larmes	tears
