Many times a disease called "telul" arises on the tip of the nose, and it grows and becomes large quickly, so that it is a noticeable thing to look at; and for this reason you must cut it off at the beginning, remove all of it, then apply a cautery or burning medicine on it; and if one delays cutting it until it is large, beware if it is hard, red in color, poor in sensation: do not touch it with iron because it is an inflamed abscess, for when it is cut sometimes great harm comes to the patient; and if the abscess is of a moist nature, not red in color, and you see that it can be completely cut out, then empty the patient and cut it without fear, and treat the area with drying and constricting substances.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	When the nose is cut and sewn.
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	Know that when solutions of continuation come into one of these cartilaginous works, it profits little, for in some men.
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	It is then necessary when this happens to someone, to examine if the wound is fresh and full of blood; and then join the two edges with a stitch, then treat it until it heals; and if the edges are already separated on one side and the other, you must then peel all parts from their surface until they heal, then bring together the two edges with a stitch, and bind them tightly, sprinkle dragon's blood powder and ground incense over it; and put a piece of strong plaster or another adhesive plaster over the powders, and leave it until it falls off by itself, then treat it with ointment until it heals.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The method of stitching is that you assemble the solution: with needles, just as we have said in the stitching of the belly; or with thread, just as I have made known to you.
des apostemes des levres	of abscesses of the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many men have within their lips hard abscesses, resembling grains of wheat, and smaller and larger; then you should turn the lips, and cut above each knot, and take them with tweezers and cut in each part; then apply the area after the incision with ground vitriol until the blood is stilled; and then wash it with oil, and treat the area with dry things until it is healed.
de la char des gencives	of the gum flesh
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Many times a flesh grows on the gums that the ancients call «albulus»; you must hold it with tweezers and cut it at its root, and let the pus or blood flow; then apply ground vitriol or other binding and drying powders to the site; if this flesh returns after cutting, which often happens, cut it a second time and cauterize it: it does not return after cautery; these are the forms of instruments for cutting.
des sordens	of the stenches
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	Sometimes there are gathered at the head of the teeth, inside the mouth between the gums, shells that are ugly and rough; and sometimes the teeth are black and yellow and green, until corruption comes to the gum, and the teeth stink; you must make the patient sit between your hands, and his head be in your lap, and scrape the teeth or the shells that appear, until nothing remains; and thus do with the blackness and the greenness, and the yellowness and other stains, until they are clean; if what is there can be removed at first attempt, it is good; if not, then repeat on the second day and the third, until you have scraped everything off; and know that teeth require various forms of instruments for scraping, according to what the work demonstrates, because the scrapers with which one scrapes between the teeth have different shapes than those with which one scrapes outside the teeth; and these forms and others should be prepared with you.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	When you treat the tooth for its pain, you should delay extracting it as long as you can, for no one should do so; for it is a very high substance up until such time that there is no excuse for scraping.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	Then when the patient is forced to extract, you must be certain of the painful tooth.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Often the pain deceives the patient, and they believe it is in the healthy tooth, and have the good tooth extracted; yet the pain does not leave because of this, until the bad one is drawn, for we have already seen this happen to these wise men; and when you are certain of the painful tooth, then you must cut around the tooth with a strong instrument all the way to the gum on all sides; then move it with your hands or with fine tongs little by little until it is well loosened, then firmly secure the tongs; and let the head of the patient be in your lap between your knees, and hold it well so that it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	After pull the tooth straight without breaking it, and if it does not come out easily, take one of these instruments and push inside on each side gently, and move it as you did first.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	And if the tooth is perforated and decayed, it is necessary that you fill it with cloths where the holes are; and then grasp it subtly with tweezers so that it does not break when pulling; and one must work very carefully around the gum to loosen the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	And be careful not to break it and leave a part behind, which may cause the patient, by the maliciousness of the root, greater pains than before.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And be wary not to act as ignorant surgeons do, who by their haste and boldness sometimes break the tooth, and do not administer what we have mentioned; but sometimes cause great illness through the extraction of roots that remain or teeth they break, as we have often seen. And when the tooth is drawn, wash the area with wine or oil and salt; and if bleeding occurs, which often happens, apply the area with ground vitriol; and if that does not work, cauterize it.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The forms of the instruments with which one moves the teeth first should have long points and thick handles, that they do not double when you pull the tooth; and these are the forms:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And they should have thick parts so that they do not bend when pulling, and they should be made of good iron, and they should be toothed to hold the teeth firmly.
de la racine des dens	of the root of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	When the root remains after pulling, it is necessary that you put on the place cotton moistened in butter for one or two days.
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	until the area is softened, then use the forceps which are called "algefri," which resemble a chicken's beak; and they should be made inside like a file, and this is the form:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not want to come out entirely with these forceps, then you must uncover all the flesh around the root, and put in the instrument which is called "althali", that is to say a spatula, of which this is the form:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And let it be strong and thick so that it does not break, and if the root jumps out because of this, it is good; if not, then help yourself with all the instruments, whose forms come hereafter:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait II rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And one makes use of this instrument which has two prongs, of which the form is here:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other tools which are mentioned earlier in the discussion of teeth, and of this instrument which resembles large forceps, of which the form is here:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And let this instrument be strong so that it cannot break, and know that many instruments for teeth exist; and also other instruments, which are not mentioned; and the wise subtle masters find their own instrument by themselves according to what their work and the diseases show them, because there are such diseases where the ancients taught no instrument due to the diversity of men; and if one breaks any part of the cartilage or other bones where it might, then search for the instruments that are necessary, which I have told you, and help yourself with gestures, of which here is the form:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And let them be thick and well-holding to grasp the bone so that it does not slip away but can hold and remove it; and then restore the place with appropriate medicines, and if there is putrefaction in the bone and it is small, then scrape it all with this instrument:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a I petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the teeth appear not according to the natural body and the form is ugly, and especially in unmarried women, then you must know if the tooth has come after the tooth, and it is not in the right place, and it cannot be smoothed or filed: then break it; and if it is loose with the tooth, take this instrument whose form is here, and it resembles a small beak, and let it be of iron and very sharp at the end.
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And the cutting little by little over several days because of the hardness of the tooth, and so that you do not move the others, and if it is visible that it can be filed, then file it with a file like the form here:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	and it is also like the file with which needles are made; and file the tooth little by little over several days lightly, so that it does not move until it falls; then smooth it at the end with any razor, and if the tooth is too sharp and it wounds the tongue, then file down the roughness until it is even, so that it does not wound the tongue or corrupt speech.
quant li dent lochent	when the teeth loosen
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	when the front teeth loosen, either by impact or by falling, and the patient cannot chew without them falling out, and you have treated them with constricting medicines, but it does not help; then they must be bound with a gold thread, for silver threads turn green and decay, but gold never changes; and let the thread be neither too thick nor too thin according to the space between the teeth; and if you wish to align the teeth, take the thread and place it double between two healthy teeth, then insert the fingers between the loose teeth, whether one or more, until you reach wisely up to the other side's healthy tooth; then begin the winding again until the part where you started, and withdraw your hand subtly and wisely so that nothing moves; and let the binding be at the root of the tooth so it cannot escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	Then cut the thread of the tooth with pliers, and join them, and place them between the healthy teeth, and put it in such a way that it does not hurt the tongue; and then leave it as tight as it can stay, and if it loosens or the thread breaks, tighten it with another thread; it will remain and serve this way for all its time, and this is the form of the teeth and the shape of the arrangement of the two healthy teeth, and the two molars, as you see:
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when the tooth falls out, it is reset in its place fresh and fresh, as we have said; and no one who is not wise and skilled should intervene, and sometimes the shape of a cow's bone tooth is made, and it is placed where the deficiency is, and it is tightened as we have said, and it remains and serves for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	to cut the tie of the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	Sometimes this tie that comes under the tongue is natural, which one is born with; or by accident from a healed wound; and the work is such that you operate on the patient’s mouth, and have his head in your lap, and lift up the tongue; then cut the nervous tie widely so that the tongue is freed from its place, and if there is hardness or knot, and it is from the healing of a wound, then use the forceps and cut the tie widely; and be careful that the incision is not too deep for the artery which is underneath; and when you have done this, clean the area with rose water and alum, or cold water, then place under the tongue a linen tent; and the patient should change it every night so that the wound does not heal.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	And if bleeding occurs, put ground vitriol on the place; and if the blood does not stop, then cauterize it with a lentigo-cautery, which is good for this; then treat it with another treatment until it heals.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see it of fistula color or black or hard, so that the patient does not feel it, do not touch it at all, for it is a chancre; and if it declines to blennorrhoea and there is moisture, then throw on an ointment, and cut it with a subtle spatula, and deliver it from one side to another; and if the blood does not stop due to your work, put ground vitriol on until it is stopped, then return to your work until you draw all pus; then lift the place of ash and salt, and treat it with other treatments until it heals.
des apostemes de la gorge	of the abscesses of the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	Sometimes there come into the throat swellings which are called "godath", and they are properly called the two almonds, and when you treat them, as we have said in the division, and if they are not healed, then beware: if it is a hard abscess of little sense and of flesh color, do not touch it with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	And if it is red and the root is large, do not touch it with iron, also for the flow of blood; but leave it until it becomes ripe, and then you will divide it, or it would break by itself; and if it is of white color turning, and the root is fine, have the instrument ready to cut, but first check if the warm abscess rests and is calmed.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	Then make the patient sit facing the sun, and his shoulders be in your hands, and work the mouth and let the surgeon hold it between his hands, and press the tongue below with all the instrument, of which this is the form; and it should be of silver or fine brass like a knife:
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	When you press the tongue with all this instrument, and you see the abscess, then take the lancet and put it in the almond, and draw it up above as much as you can; and draw some threads out with it, then cut it with the instrument, of which this is the form, that resembles forceps; and the ends are curved, one towards the other, and they are very sharp, and it is made of iron or steel:
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument present, then cut it with pliers, of which here is the form:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les II amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les II amandres igament.	And let it be sharp on one side and blunt on the other; and when you have cut one of the almonds, then cut the other in the same manner, and after the incision gargle the patient with warm water, and water and salt, and if bleeding occurs, then gargle the patient with water in which pomegranate rinds are boiled, or myrtle leaves, and similar things, until the blood is stopped; then cure it until it is healed; and sometimes other abscesses besides the two almonds grow in the throat, so cut them in the same way as the two almonds.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	And I treated a woman who had an abscess grow inside her throat, that is to say an abscess of the little sense; and it had almost completely closed off her throat, so that the woman could not breathe because the passage was blocked, and she could neither eat nor drink, and she would have died if she remained thus for one or two days.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscess had grown so much that it had forced open two veins through the two passages of the nose.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	I hastened then at once, and inserted one ounce in one nostril, then I pulled it out, and drew a large portion of the pus; then I repeated this on the other nostril, and opened his mouth and pressed his tongue; afterwards, I inserted the ounce into these abscesses, and cut away a part, and only a little blood came out; and thus was relieved the conduit in the woman's throat, and she began now to drink water and then wine, and I did not stop cutting this abscess for a long time; and the abscess continued to grow again, filling the place that I had emptied, until it became very large; then I drained it and cauterized it inside the throat: thus it remained without growing; and I left those parts, and do not know what God did with her after me.
de l’uve	of the grape
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	When rheum descends to the grape, and it is swollen and elongated, it is called "perpendicular"; and if it is below, large and round, it is called "grape".
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	When it is treated as we have said in the division, and the treatment does not help, and you see that the red abscesses are calmed, and they are thin, then you must cut them; and those which are roundly gathered and are not elongated; and they are blood-colored or of a flesh color or black, then you must avoid incising them.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great danger to the patient.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	So then, when you see it, according to the manner that I have said, of its blennorrhea and length, you make the patient sit before the sun, and press his tongue with the instrument we mentioned earlier; then insert the needle into the grape, and pull it down, and cut it with one of the two instruments I mentioned in the incision of the two almonds.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And you must not cut beyond the excess that is over the natural limit; for if you cut more, you harm the voice and speech; and after the incision, use what we have said in the incision of the two almonds, and treat it until it heals.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the patient fears the cutting, then you must use ingenuity in the cautery of such fear.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	And the manner of the cautery is sharp.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	And it is that the patient puts his head in your hand, and then you press his tongue with the instrument we have mentioned in the chapter on cautery, and mix with hot vinegar that is not too thick nor too thin; and use the application of this instrument, of which here is the form:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés IIII jors ou V Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And it should have on the head a bristle where one puts the medicine, like the bristles of a spoon, and place the instrument with all the medicine on the eye; and let the patient lie on his side so that saliva and phlegm flow from his mouth due to the medicine inside, so that it does not descend into the throat and harm him; then hold your hand over all the medicine and press it onto the eye for about half an hour until you see it withered and the irritation from the medicine subsides; and if you wish, take cotton and wrap it around any instrument, moisten the cotton in the medicine, and insert the instrument wrapped in the cotton into the canal above so that the cotton burns on the eye; do this often until the cautery is perfect, then leave it to dry, and it will fall off after four or five days. And if you need to restart the cautery with the medicine, start again, and afterwards cautery around the eye with cotton soaked in butter, and clean what is around from the medicine; and let it be washed with cold water, and treated with gargles until it is healed.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en I pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait I estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This cure is more valuable than incision or cautery; if it is treated by fumigation in this manner, take calamus and hyssop and oregano and rue and chamomile and horehound and similar herbs, and gather all of them or some of them into a pot, and put oil into it, and make it boil; and the pot should be well sealed with strong clay, and in the middle of the pot have the instrument placed according to this manner:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	And it should be of silver or bronze, and one of the pipes placed in the mouth of the patient so that the vapor rises to the ear through the tube until the ear is mortified; after that repeat often, until the ear dries, and take care not to do this at the beginning of the onset of a hot abscess, for many things happen; and do not perform this except when the hot abscess is declining.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	And if this instrument is not present, take a cane and put inside the head an eggshell, so that the mouth of the patient is not too hot; for the eggshell does not allow the steam to make the mouth heavy, and it is a good treatment altogether safe.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou I morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge I fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren I estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Often a fish bone or spine, or some other thing, gets stuck in the throat; therefore, you should pull out what you can see and press the tongue to the sun with all the instrument so that you can move the object; and for what is not visible and is lodged in the throat, you must make the patient vomit before the food is cooked in the stomach; perhaps the stuck thing will come out through vomiting; or have the patient swallow a piece of sponge, or a piece of navel, or a lettuce root, or a piece of dry bread; and tie a string to the sponge, then swallow it; when it reaches the place, it will stick, and then you pull it out; and if it does not come out by what we have said, take an instrument like this:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	And let the instrument be curved at the head so that it can more easily enter the throat, and have the head lifted up; and beware that you do not touch the epiglote, lest he choke or push the bone inside; and it is better that the patient insert the instrument himself so that he moves where the thing is pierced; then he pushes down, pulling firmly with all the instrument evenly until it is firm.
de la sansue de la gorge	of the phlegm from the throat
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	Sometimes the phlegm is treated with medicine, as I have said in the division, by the care of medicines; and when this does not help, then look into the patient's throat in the sunlight, after which you press their tongue with the instrument that I have told you about.
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	And if you see the pus, then draw it all with a small hook or with subtle tweezers that are suitable for this.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	And if this does not work, then take a hairy cord, and put it in the patient's throat, then place a heated iron on the movement of the cord, and do this often.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	And if the patient is plagued by water all day.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	then take a full glass of cold water, and work it in the mouth, and throw it down to swallow, and move it often with his hand; and as soon as the pus feels the water, it falls.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	And if it does not fall as we have said, then sub-fumigate the patient with asafoetida, with the instrument that I have mentioned in the fumigation of the grape; do this many times, for it will fall without delay.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	And the manner of fumigation is that you take a pot in which there are live coals, and the pot is covered with a cover pierced in the middle, and in that hole be the head of the instrument; then throw your fumigation in it, and the patient puts the head of the cane in his mouth, and closes the mouth so that no smoke comes out but goes to the phlegm; and the phlegm will now fall, and if it does not fall, repeat the fumigation several times; and let the patient feel thirsty, and eat salty and hot things, and drink no water; and then it is necessary for it to go out by this treatment.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And the form of the instrument with which one draws out phlegm is, when it can be seen, similar to curved tweezers for easily entering the throat; and it resembles a bird’s beak, and has roughness like a file, so that what it grasps, it cannot release; and you see here its form:
li chapistres des apostemes	the chapter of abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	There are many kinds of abscesses, according to what the memory comes after one and another in this book, and they differ in perforation and size; and it is in two ways, one of which is in its own appearance, and from what it holds moisture.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And the second way is for the places where they are on the body.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	for the abscess of the head is different from that of the fundament, and the abscess of the fleshy part is different from that which comes in joints, and each has its own judgment in the work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	And there are abscesses that one should not pierce until the pus is ripe according to its completion; and there are such that must be pierced when they are hard, and do not die according to their completion, like abscesses that are near joints.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	For when abscesses come near joints, and it is left until it swells around, by chance the ligaments and nerves of the joint are corrupted, which causes contraction in that limb.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	For when the abscess is near the main limb, and if you delay perforation until it is dead, it will harm the main limb; if it is near the fundament, it should be pierced before it becomes dead; and it is not right to pierce a hard abscess without complete digestion, except for one near the fundament, which might swell and extend inward, leading to a fistula; and cannot heal over a long term.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And you must know the time for perforating an abscess that is ready according to completion, and this is when the pain is calmed, and the departure of fever, and the lessening of the pain and redness, and from the weakening and sharpening of the top of the abscess, and other signs; and you must make the perforation at the lowest part of the abscess where it appears moist; and let the perforation be lengthwise on the body, and if the abscess is in the hands or feet, or in joints and nerves and arteries, and in all similar places where there is no pus.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	In those that bend, according to that limb.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when abscesses are in a soft place, it is better that you leave the perforation until it is confirmed after complete digestion, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	For if you pierce it before that, the body of the venom from it will be prolonged, and it is full of much filth; and by chance the lips and the depths of it may harden.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And there are some abscesses that should be pierced according to the size of the body, according to what the limb requires.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	And you should make small perforations in small abscesses; and in large abscesses, large perforations, and many slits according to the likeness of the size of the abscess; and there are such abscesses where it is necessary to shave the core and cut; when it has become as yellow as drapery and is softened, you should do as with buboes: and there are those that are slit in three angles, and there are those which are cut like the leaf of myrtle, as angre abscesses; and there are those where a round cut is made, and other cuts and similar incisions.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	Those who have no head, such as a superficial abscess, you must pierce it completely; and when the abscess is large, and it has collected much pus, and you pierce it, do not draw out all the pus at that hour, but draw out part of it; then plug the abscess until the next day, then draw out some more; do this many times in small amounts, until all the pus comes out; similarly if the patient is of weak strength, or a pregnant woman, or young children, or old decrepit men.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	For the spasm sometimes occurs with the discharge of the pus, which may cause the patient to die, and you do not perceive it.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Avoid therefore this chapter with great caution, and when you have pierced the abscess, wipe the wound, and look if the opening of the abscess is small; and if it is a smooth surface, then apply lint or old cotton; and if it is a large abscess, and there are many openings, then you must place a tent in each one so that they come against each other; and if you have cut into the skin part of the abscess and you have shaved around it, then you must fill it with old cotton or linen wool without moisture, and bind it until the third day; then remove it, and treat it with ointment until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	And if bleeding occurs in your work, then administer cold water and ash, and wet the cloth, and place it on the bleeding area multiple times.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the bleeding persists, then administer treatment and care, and the powders that I have mentioned in their places in this book, and if it is winter time, and the place where the abscess is very nervous, you must put on cloths wet in wine and hot oil; and if it is summer, and the area is fleshy, you must put on cloths wet in water and oil, or in cold wine and oil, up to the third day, as we have said; and then lance the abscess, wipe and treat it, as appropriate, until it is healed.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	And this must be understood universally in the treatment of abscesses: now I have told you how one should proceed with the treatment of abscesses, and here is the chapter.
des soros	of the sewers
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	When small abscesses come from the head, and they are kinds of growths that are in layers, like the comb of a hen, and there are many similarities.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	There are some that are fatty and of such which have moisture like flesh; and there are those which are hard and stony to cut, and there is no doubt if the artery does not hinder.
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	And the work of the waist is that you test with all the instrument which is called "introducer," of which the form comes after, what it contains.
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	For if it contains moisture, then cut it open on top of the length.
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	And when the moisture is emptied, then peel without leaving any of the skin that contains that moisture, for it returns immediately if anything is left; then soak cotton in Egyptian ointment, if it is present; if not, in water and salt, and apply it to the wound, and leave it until the next day; and this will cure what remains from the night.
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then restart the cotton, as before, on the second day, and the third, until you know well that nothing of the night remains; then treat the wound with an appropriate ointment until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	And if the abscess holds fat, cut it according to this form, lengthwise; and throw in your lancets, and scrape it from all sides, and apply all your care to draw out the cloth where it lies; and if the artery opposes you, do what I have said after.
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	And do the same for the abscess if it is stony, and in cutting and cleaning as I have told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	And cut into the stony and moist abscess, it is lighter, for they are full of blood.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	And some of these abscesses on the head have no moisture, and of those there were the abscesses that I cut on the head of an old woman; and I found the abscess like a dull stone, rough and white, and could not be broken; and if one had struck any part of it, they would have made as much injury as with a stone.
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	In other abscesses coming to the head, whether those that come at the top of children's heads and at the roots of the ears, the opening should always be at the lowest point, for pus to flow out; and treat them as is appropriate.
des scrophules	Of the scrofula
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	Often this abscess occurs at the neck, and beneath the jawbones, and in the armpits, and sometimes they appear elsewhere on the body, and they are large, and they cluster together.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	And each scrofula is properly within its coat, like the knot and the abscess of the head, as we have said; and the forms of these scrofulas are many.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	There are such that contain moisture, and there are malignant ones that do not wish to obey health.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	In that one then which you see of good disposition to the touch, and is similar in color to the skin, and moves on all sides and is not adhered to the nerves of the neck nor to the artery nor to the conduit, and is not deep; it is necessary that you cut over it, and peel from each part, and stretch the two lips of the sore with hooks if you need them, as we have said in abscesses of the head; and draw out bit by bit, and be sure that you do not cut the nerve nor the vein, and let not the scalpel be sharp or cutting, so that your hand does not slip, and do not go too deep, that you may not cut what you should not.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	And if you cut the vein or artery, and this does not allow you to work, put in the wound vitriol powder, or some powders that stop blood, and hold the wound; and leave it until the abscess is calmed, and the wound softened, and begins to heal.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	And when the blood is stanched, return to your work until you complete it; then seek out any small remaining scabs, cut them and clean them.
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	And if there is a large vein at the root of the scab, you should not cut that scab at its root, but tie it with a strong double thread, and let it fall out on its own without harm; then apply the wound with old cotton soaked in Egyptian ointment, then treat it.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	And if you cut all the scrofula, then you must bring together the two lips of the wound, and sew them now, since there is no remaining excess due to the size of the scrofula.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	and you must pay attention to cut the root of it, and pull hard, and sew it as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Those scrofulas that hold excess, pierce them where it appears to die; and pierce them thus as the one previously mentioned, hanging down, then apply tents with ointment and similar things, so that it corrupts what remains of the corruption; and when the wound is well cleaned, treat it with healing ointment until it is healed.
de squinance	of strain
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The ancient spoke of the cutting of the throat; but I have never seen it done in our land, and this is the writing of their words.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en II amandres.	For those who have strain, it is necessary that the slit of the throat which is called "epiglote" be cleared; and if no help is given by this, because all the veins and the breath of the patient are affected in those who have a hot abscess in the mouth, or in the throat or in the two tonsils.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the disease is in the channel of the breath, it is necessary to cut the epiglote to avoid the loss that comes from strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige; et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	It is then necessary, when we wish to split the epiglote, that we split it below three circles or four a small slit across, between the two circles or by the quantity of the slit from the surface, not in the cartilage; and this place is suitable for the section of the epiglote that there is no flesh, and the vessels are long to inquire.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit; et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix; et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	And if the master is fearful, then he must stretch the skin of the throat to the whole inch, then split the heart until it comes to the windpipe; and avoid the blood vessels, if you see anything, and then cut the surface, as we have said; and it is demonstrated by the section of the phlegm from the windpipe that flows out through the place which is broken, and by the loss of voice; and leave the wound open for a while.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les II levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the hour has passed in which one fears strangulation, bring together the two lips of the wound from the neck, and sew them all alone without cartilage; then administer medicines that cause flesh to grow until it is healed.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Albucasis says that one should not do this until the throat is entirely compressed, and the patient is judged to be dying, and the defect increases.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort; et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee; et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	Then one cuts the epiglottis so that the patient cannot swallow, and he breathes through the wound, and thus is saved from death; and for this reason the ancients commanded to leave the wound open until the malice of the disease passes, and it passes in three days or four. And then they commanded to sew up the wound and clean it until it was cleansed; and I will tell you what I saw.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon; et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	I saw that a young lady took a knife and stuck it in her throat, cutting part of the uvula; and I was called to treat her, and found her as if dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I uncovered the wound and found the blood that had come out of it, and I knew she had not cut any vein or artery in her throat, and the air was escaping through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee; et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition; por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	I hurried and sewed up the wound, and treated it until it was healed; and nothing happened to the young lady except that her voice became hoarse, and she later returned to normal; for this reason, I say that there should be no fear in surgery on the epiglottis.
de la grosse gorge	of the large throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes; et est selonc II manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	This abscess is called "throat hernia," and it is a large abscess in the color of jaiss, and it mostly affects women; and it comes in two ways: natural, and accidental; the natural one has no sign.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere; et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire: se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point; et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And the accidental one is of two kinds, of which one resembles fatty nodules, and the other kind resembles an abscess that comes from arterial nodes; and there is fear, and it is not fitting to work with fire except in the small one, and you prove and search through the entire insertion: if you find it like a fat knot, and it cannot go into any vein, then cut it as you would cut nodules, and extract all its covering, if there is any; and thoroughly investigate, and treat it as necessary until it is perfectly healed.
des nous	from us
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances; et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	Many methods from us exist, of which I will speak all the similarities; and now it is fitting that I tell all the differences that are between wound and discharge.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that discharge is heat and fever lasting until the boiling over has passed, and the putrefaction is complete; then the fever and heat subside.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros; et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	With the wound, there is neither heat nor fever nor pain, and it contains a surface, which is its own sac and is according to the color of the body, and begins like a blister, and becomes large; and they are according to two similarities, either dry or moist, and their colors are as I have said in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	It is necessary, when you come to the treatment of the wound, that you test and inquire first about all the instrument which is called “introducer”, according to what its form will come in the chapter which follows.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme; puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	And the method of inquiring about abscesses of the nose is that you take the moistest place you find in the abscess, and turn your fingers little by little, until you know that the instrument has pierced the core, according to the size of the abscess; then withdraw the introducer, and be careful in this that it does not become worse.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes; et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout; et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	If running moisture comes out, whatever color it has, cut it as I have said for other abscesses; and if no moisture follows the introducer, know that it is fatty, then cut it in a cross shape, take it with forceps, and peel it lightly from each side and watch the clot where it lies so you draw it out clean with the wound; and if you cannot draw it out clean, draw it out in pieces so that nothing remains.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois; et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	For if anything remains there, the swelling returns many times; and if a little remains and causes pain, use some corrosive powders on the wound, bind the wound, apply things to soothe a hot abscess, and treat it with other treatments until it is healed; and if the swelling is large, sew the two edges of the wound together, and treat it with what promotes flesh growth.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet II jors ou III, tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	And if the vein that beats is contrary or otherwise troubles you, hasten and use ground vitriol instead, leave it for two or three days until the wound becomes rotten, and stop the boiling of the blood; then return to copper what remains of the swelling.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule; et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule; et sont de III manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	See here the forms of the instruments for insertion, and they are of three types: large, medium, and small; and there are three squares called "albaret," and one called "breb," and there are of three types: large, medium, and small, to encircle abscesses of fistulas; and they resemble the needles used to sew snares, and they can be made of brass yellow, or iron, or silver, and those that are yellow are more valuable, and black plumb is more tested for encircling the sores of fistulas; and they come in three types: large, medium, and small, according to the width of the openings.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi; et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	The forms of the lancets are very similar, as you see here: large, medium, and small; and there are lancets that have two curves in three ways also; and there are lancets that have three curves, and they too are in three ways; and there are lancets that have two curves, and lancets with only one curve, and they are of three ways; and all these are necessary in their place.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf; et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes; et sont de III manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois; et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus; et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	The head of these is sharp where one cuts, and there are some that do not cut well from one side, which are used to peel the skin so as not to cut the vein or nerve; and among these introductories are the lancets placed in sleeves, so that the patient does not feel them at the opening of abscesses; and they are of three ways: large, small, and medium, as you see; and they are only used in fleshy places, such as legs, arms, breasts, and similar areas; and sometimes one makes another instrument small, resembling peelings of rushes, according to this form, with which one stops bleeding.
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	and it is placed sometimes at the place that heals with cutting of veins, and arteries, and sometimes according to this large form:
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme; et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	sometimes the breasts of some men swell when they begin to be corrupted, until they resemble a woman's breasts; and they remain ugly and swollen, and whoever wants to treat them must thread according to this form from line .b. up to .g.:
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures; de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.; puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif; et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	then peel the fat, and apply medicine to the wound to heal flesh, then sew together the two lips of the wound, and treat it until it is healed; and if the breast sags downward and becomes soft due to its size as happens with women, cut it in two sides from above, by two similar incisions; so that one should be attached to the other at the end of each, so that the larger line contains the smaller according to this form, from this line .b. up to the line .g.; then peel the skin between the two lips, remove the fat, and administer what we have said about sewing and powders, and whatever is necessary in the treatment until it is healed; and if it is not healed or the incision is not fully made because the patient does not want to rest or due to bleeding, you must fill the wound with moist cotton in a corrosive ointment; leave it until it consumes the remaining fat, then treat it until it is healed.
des apostemes des asselles	of the abscesses of the armpits
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	These abscesses that come under the armpits are kinds of hard scrofula with edges, and some contain moisture.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Those that contain moisture should be cut according to this form, from line .b. up to line .g.:
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when all the pus that is in the abscess is emptied, apply the wound with old cotton, and leave it until the next day, then remove all the cotton, and treat with an appropriate ointment until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscess is of the appearance of scrofula, then cut it as we have said in the incisions for scrofula, and if the wound emits pus, then apply cauterization as we have said before.
de la routure de l’artere	of the rupture of the artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme; et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont; et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans; et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.
