When the artery is ruptured, and the skin above is sealed, there often come abscesses, and this also happens with swollen veins and abscesses; and it is recognized thus when it is due to the artery, then the abscesses are long in appearance; and when you feel them with your hands, you sense the constriction; and when it is due to the vein, there is a round swelling visible; and it is folly to cut this abscess, especially when it is under the ribs and at angles and on the neck and in many other places, and it is very dangerous.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc; puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte; puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples; puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme; puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient; puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit; puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil; et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus; puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez; puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	It is then necessary to avoid the iron treatment, and that which is at the head must be avoided as well, and in those who have an artery swelling, cut through the skin above; then work the incision with lancets, and carefully separate the artery from the tissues until it is uncovered; then place a needle underneath it, and make it pierce to the other side, and tie the artery with a double thread in two places according to what I have taught you in the extraction of the two arteries that are in temples; then puncture the area between the two knots with an intramuscular needle until the blood comes out which is there, and let the abscess be released; then apply the treatment that induces vomiting until the knots fall off; then treat it with a dressing suitable for this condition, until it heals; and if the abscess is as large as the vein, you must touch with your hand what you can of the abscess to the whole skin, then place the needle underneath where you hold in your hand, and make it pierce, and there should be a double thread so that you pull from the other side; then tie the abscess as I have said, or tie one end of the two parts with both ends of the thread; and if you fear that the threads will not come out, place another needle with all the thread underneath the entire abscess at the incision of the first needle, and tie the threads in four places; then cut open the abscess until the excess comes out, then remove the excess from the heart and leave what is tied; then put on a cloth moistened in wine and oil, then give it treatments with bandages and ointments until it heals.
des apostemes des ners	of abscesses of nerves
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	Just as abscesses come in the artery and vein, abscesses come to the nerves when they are wounded, or by too great labor, and similar things.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor; et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur; et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction; et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	And this happens more often in the shoulders and hands and all places where there are joints, and it is grievous abscesses, and its color resembles the color of the flesh, and it is in various positions without pain; and when it is squeezed forcefully, then the patient feels pain, and it is not entirely within the body but beneath the skin; and it moves well from all sides, and does not go forward or backward, nor downward or upward, and that which is in joints should not be cut with iron: perhaps contraction might occur; and those that are on the head or forehead, cut the skin with a lancet.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine; et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the abscess is small, hold it with tweezers and cut it at its root; and if it is large, suspend it with a lancet, then scrape it, remove it, and sew up the wound, treating it until it heals.
des grosses boces pendans	large hanging boils
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans; et je vis I home qui en avoit II ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	Sometimes it happens in the belly and not elsewhere, which is a disease called "fungus" due to its resemblance to mushrooms, and its roots are subtle, and the heads are large; and there are small ones and very large ones; and I saw one person who had two in their belly that resembled fungi more than anything else, with no difference, and they were white, and had fine roots, and were split open, and a moisture would flow out immediately.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un XVIII onces pesant, et en l’autre VI З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine; si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu.	I cut them and found one weighing eighteen ounces, and the other six and a half. The work in the incision is such that you observe if the patient is moist, and the color of the joint is white and moist and of subtle root; then cut it with a wide spatula, and have the cautery at hand by the fire.
Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer; et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent I fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse II jors; et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet, puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	For in cutting often comes too great a flow of blood, and if the blood overcomes you, then hasten to cauterize; and if you see the patient frightened and fearful of the iron incision, take well-made linen thread, and bind the joint as we have said, and leave it for two days; then rebind it, and do not stop tightening the linen thread until you cut the joint, and it will fall off by itself without effort; and if the roots are large, there is fear in cutting them directly for the belly, but you can well cut half of it, then cauterize so that it does not return; then clean the wound, and be careful not to cut the skin which is red in color and thin with little feeling.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	For this is an abscess with a sore, and I will come to the treatment of sores later.
quant li boude ist fuer	When the boil is ready to burst.
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit; et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	If the appearance of the boil comes from a wound cautery or a tear in the skin, and it is on the belly where some boils occur, as happens with other ruptures, or from blood that flows from veins or arteries as mentioned before, or from flatulence; and if it is due to a rupture in the skin and an opening of the boil, then the color of the abscess resembles the color of the body, and it is a light matter without pain, and opens with various outlets.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it is due to the opening of the intestine, then it is more varied, and when you press it with your fingers, it sinks in and then returns, and sometimes it becomes hard, and greatly expands at the entrance of the bath and from strenuous work.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit; et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	And if it is due to moisture, it is a light thing, and it opens well when you press it with your hand, without constraining; and if it is due to blood, then the abscess opens by these signs large and hard, and is fixed according to a quantity; and if it is due to windiness, then it is soft to touch, and the work is such that you look at whether the appearance is due to arterial blood or vein blood or windiness.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure.	So you must leave the treatment.
Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	For there is doubt and fear, as I have said in the chapter about abscesses, concerning the artery and the vein.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude; puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains, puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile, puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine; puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz; puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine; se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre; et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit; et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren II aguilles, et i boute II fors filz, et boute les II aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier; puis estrain l’aposteme en IIII leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi; ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit; et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	And if the appearance is due to intestine or pus, you must instruct the patient to lie on their back, stretched out straight, then apply a bandage all around the swelling; then command them to lie between your hands, then go all around the area that you have bandaged with lint, then stretch half of the abscess above with a large scalpel; then bind it tightly around with a strong thread or rope made of thick silk and make sure the knot is secure; then work on the stretched part of the abscess over the binding, and put your finger in to seek out the intestine; if you find it caught in the binding, untie it, and bring the intestine up above the belly; and if you find pus, take it with a scalpel, and cut away the excess; and if an artery or vein opposes you, move gently around it, then return to your work and take two needles, put two strong threads through them, and place the two needles in cross formation where you have pierced; then draw out the abscess at four points over the needles, and when you see, remove the needles, and leave the area until it becomes pus-filled, and dead flesh will fall off on its own; or cut it away when it is fine and rotten, then treat the area as needed, and close the abscess as we have said; draw out the blood or moisture that you find, then clean the area as needed, and suture the wound.
dou chancre	of the ulcer
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	We have discussed in the division the likenesses of ulcers, and how one should treat them with medicines, and how one should avoid iron cure; and we speak of an ulcer appearing in the thigh, and great caution is needed in its treatment, and the ancients said that when ulcers are in a place where they can be scraped off like ulcers which are on the breasts, and in the groin, and in similar places, it must be completely removed when it begins; and when it is large and old, you should not approach it, for I have never been able to heal any; no one has ever healed them before me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide I boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the work, when it is in a place where it can be removed, as we have said, is that you purge the patient of black bile; then make him sweat if there is obvious congestion, then prepare the patient well for the operation; then apply your knives to the ulcer, and scrape all around, and remove it entirely without leaving anything; and let the blood flow freely, and press the area with your hand or some object, and if the bleeding stops you from making an incision in the artery or vein, cauterize it until the blood is stopped; then treat it with other treatments until it is healed.
de ydropisie	of dropsy
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces II semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer: lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme:	We have already said in the division the types of dropsy, and how the accumulation of water is formed, and the signs of each type, and the cure that is performed by medicines, and that which is cured by iron: it is edema alone; and one should not touch iron on these two types: namely, tympanites and hyposarche, for it is a deadly thing; then when you treat this type of dropsy called "edema" with medicines, and the cure does not work, look if the patient is weak, or if they have another disease besides dropsy, such as fever and diarrhea and similar things; do not touch iron, for there is doubt; and if you see the patient full of strength, and they do not have any other disease but only dropsy, and they are not too young nor too old, then you must act thus: lift the patient upright on your hands, and the attendants press the abdomen pushing the water to the lowest part of the body, then take the spatholite thorny according to this form:
Et soit trenchans de II pars.	And let it be sharp from two parts.
a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier; puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines: si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude III dois droit desoz sus lou poignil; et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude III dois; et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu; puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor; puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme:	And let it be sharp, and all the way not so penetrating that it can reach the intestine when you insert it, and it should not puncture; then look if the dropsy is inclined towards the intestines: then you must cut under the belly three times straight down to the hip; and if the dropsy is due to liver disease, your incision should be on the left side of the belly three times; and if it is for the spleen, it should be on the right, and it is not suitable that the patient lies on the incision so that the superfluities do not flow to that weak spot; then pierce all the skin with the instrument, and insert it, and lift your hand to let all the fluid between the skin and the surface come out as in peeling to the quantity of a finger or around; then pierce the surface until the fluid comes to an empty place, which is where the water lies, then draw it forcefully, and insert this instrument whose form is here described:
Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz I petit pertus; et ou costeit d’une part, III pertus; et II d’autre part, et I d’autre; et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	And it is similar to a fine silver chain, and it is made of tin or light brass, and in the lower part, there is a small hole; and on one side, three holes; and two from another side, and one from another; and the head is cut like a feather, and this is the form of the incision with which the scribes cut the feather:
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument; vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort; mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz; puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere; puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit; fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue.	At the top is the alembic, so that when the instrument reaches the water, they now heat up the instrument; then empty half or a third of it, for if you empty more than necessary at this time, perhaps the patient may die from the resolution of his spirit by the remedy, or he falls into a coma, or approaches death; but empty according to the quantity of its virtue, and according to what the disposition of the patient's strength indicates, and their pulse; then draw the instrument and retain the water, and it is now retained for the cork that plugs the hole on top of the surface, which I have spoken about, that you pierce in this manner; then restart the instrument another day if you see the patient tolerating this, and draw a small quantity of water; do this for several days, and be careful not to follow until there remains but a little bit of water.
Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre; et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	And if you doubt about the patient and leave much water in him, cure it with burial or hot sand and by sweating a lot or bathing and in the sun, and dye from drinking; and cure it with drying medicines until he is healed, and cauterize on the stomach and on the liver and on the spleen after extracting the water, as I have said before.
de l’estopement de la verge	of the constriction of the penis
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu.	Sometimes children are born who have no opening in the penis, or the opening is small, or it is not in its proper place.
Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout I spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme:	It is necessary to pierce it entirely with a very fine instrument according to this form:
puis met ou pertus I clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi III jors ou IIII et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet; et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	then put in the opening a fine plug of lint, and tie it and keep it thus for three days or four, and when he wants to urinate, then remove the plug, let him urinate, and then replace it; and perhaps none is needed, because the urine that comes out does not leave it closed.
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera.	He whose opening is small, is treated with the plug of lint, as we have said, so it will widen.
Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut; et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	Those who do not have the opening in its proper place are defective, for some are born with the opening at the tip of the penis, so they cannot urinate unless they lift their penis up; and they cannot straddle because the matter cannot reach the marrow, and this is a bad disease.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient; et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the method of the work is that the patient lies often on his back, then extends the head of the rod and cuts it also like the length of a feather, so that the hole falls in the middle, as it should be; and beware of blood flow which comes often, and if it happens, stop it with what stops blood, and treat the wound until it is healed.
des pustules de la verge	pustules of the penis
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide; et en i a malignes et non malignes; si covient que tu les preignes a I oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien; puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	Often this albathe comes on the penis, and it is an ugly appearance of flesh; and there are malignant and non-malignant ones; you must take them with a fine lancet, cut and clean them all, then put moist cotton with Egyptian ointment on; then treat it with diafinicon ointment until it is healed.
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere.	And if the ulcer is malignant, of a pus-filled color and oozing, then you must apply cautery to it.
Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier; et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer.	When you have cut it, and if the ulcer is on top of the penis, with part inside the skin and part outside, then you must remove the ulcer that is inside first; and when it is sealed, then treat the part outside.
Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion; si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	For when you treat it all at once, the head of the penis is not secure and may be pierced, leading to blackening and corruption in the penis and testicles; therefore, you must remove everything that is blackened and corrupted, then apply a plaster made of honey and flour with the bark of pomegranates and violets, then treat it with other treatments until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme:	And if bleeding occurs, apply the lunar cauterization according to this form:
Li cauteres si aide as II dispositions ensamble: c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption; et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi; et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a I estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars; et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a I spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil; puis dessevre belement entre II, et i met I subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	The cautery helps in two conditions together: namely, bleeding and corruption; and if the head of the penis is corrupted and retracted, then you must put a tube of bronze into the urethra of the penis, and let the patient urinate through it; and when the foreskin is adhered to the head of the penis which happens to those who have not been circumcised, or where there is an injury or an abscess, then you must scrape it with a special instrument until the ligaments are loosened, and release the head of the penis from all sides; and if it is difficult to separate this, then you must scrape with a spatula some part of the tip of the penis and the skin; then gently separate them, and place a fine linen cloth moistened in cold water between them so that it does not adhere again.
de la circoncision	of the circumcision
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	Circumcision is not a breaking of continuity like other wounds; nevertheless, when we perform this work of our own will, and especially for children, it is necessary that we do the best work, and the least harmful to healing.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the ancients did not speak of the circumcision of their children, for they do not use it in their law, and we have nothing more than what we have acquired through experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor I dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a II toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	For I have wanted the majority of masters and surgeons who perform circumcision around the prepuce, and at the foreskin, and with an entire novacule; the blood flees because there are two layers, and perhaps one cuts the upper layer and leaves the lower one.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	Or the recovery is cut short, and the pain is doubled, and in the cleansing of the nail bed the tip of the member is not secure; and in the cleansing of the nail by chance the iron slips, and ruins the work, and often they are born thus without need for cleansing and I have wanted it.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	Of the cleansing that is done with force on all the thread of the ligament I have found the goodness of the experiment, for the force cuts just as well above as below.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en I tout soul tens; mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir; et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens; puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens; puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz I poc a I autre liien; et la tien as II dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les II liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge; puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres; et met poudre sus et sus la poudre I drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	For when you press your hand, you cut equally in the entire time; but let the thread be tightly wound around the skin; and the method of the first work is such that you make the child think, if he understands, that you are only tying the thread around the foreskin solely for this purpose, then give him hope in every way you can; then hold it straight between your hands, and place the forceps between your hands or under your feet so the child does not see them nor any of the instruments; then put your hand to the foreskin and blow on the heart, and draw it up until the head of the penis is exposed; then cleanse well of the dirt that has gathered there, then tie the tip with a double thread, then tie below the pouch to another ligature; hold it by both hands at the second ligature to the scrotum and index finger, and cut between the two ligatures, then lift the heart up quickly and pull the head of the penis; then let the blood flow little by little, for this is the best; apply powder over and over, with the powder mixed with a glue made from an egg white diluted with rose water, cooked well and fresh oil rose added, and leave it on until the next day, and treat it with further care until it heals.
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste: li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	The first form of forces for purification is this: the two shoulders should be held and be cutting, and the shoulders should also be as large as the sleeve evenly:
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision; donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme; et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	The error of purification is when the pus inside flows at the incision; then you must extend it with your nail, unless the area forms an abscess; and cut it evenly, and if you cannot hold it with your nail, then hold it with forceps, and then cut it.
Et s’il trespassent III jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement; si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	And if it lasts more than three days, and the area under the penis is swollen, then leave it until the abscess becomes cooler, and gently scrape it; cut it as much as you can move it, and be careful of the part of the penis, which will not harm it at all.
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point; cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Treat then the area of things with a hot powder plaster, which we have said in the chapter on powders, and if you cut beyond measure from the core, and it goes above, it will do no harm; treat it then as we have said until it is healed.
dou retenement de l’urine	about the retention of urine
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division; et se li urine n’est desliie , et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz; et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet; et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e; et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme: et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil; et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	Retention of urine is due to the obstruction by stones, or congealed blood, or feces, or dead flesh, or similar things that we have mentioned in the division; and if the urine is not released, and you see that it is retained because of a stone that is in or at the neck of the bladder, then the patient should be bent over his knees; and their feet should be placed on their back, extending their belly from the upper part towards the back, and restrain the patient as tightly as they can; and thus the neck of the bladder is forced to expel the stone above, by which the urine is released; and if it does not come out, as we have said, and the patient feels great pain, then you must administer extraction with all the instrument called "catheter," of which this is the form: and it should be made of fine thin silver wire, like a bird's feather; and its tube should be one and a half palms long, and it should be thin at the tip.
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren I fil double, et lie au chief I poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue; et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus I siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede; puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude; puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors; puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine; et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	And the method of the release of the urine is that you take a double thread, and tie at the end a ball of wool or cotton, and put the end of the thread inside the catheter; and cut the excess wool and put it up to the tip of the catheter, then anoint the catheter with oil or butter and egg white, and have the patient sit on the chair, and wash the bladder and the penis with moist oil and olive oil and warm water; then gently insert the catheter into the penis until it reaches the root of the penis, then double the penis upwards towards the belly; then push the catheter forward up to the bladder, and feel the patient come until the empty part is reached, and this is not done according to this order because the tube or it goes is twisted; then stretch the thread with all the wool little by little, and the urine follows the wool, then pull out forcefully, and let the urine flow; and repeat the catheterization until the bladder is emptied, and the patient is relieved.
des maladies de la vessie	diseases of the bladder
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When blood comes into the bladder or putrefaction is gathered there, and you see aqueous and medicinal substances distill, then make use of all the instrument which is called "clepsydre", and it is of this form:
Elle est close, et si a III pertus: II d’une part, et I d’autre, si com tu vois; et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est; et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens; si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens; si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie: si est ci:	It is closed and has three openings: two on one side and one on the other, as you see; and the end should be such that the medicine can plug the penis well without addition, so that one may draw moisture and push when necessary; and when you wish to introduce your medicines into the bladder, put the head of the tube in the liquid, and pull with the syringe inside; thus you will draw the liquid into the syringe, and then push hard again with the plunger inside; then the liquid will enter and come to the bladder now so that the patient can feel it; and this is the form of the subtle clyster with which one clysters the bladder: it is here:
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut; et desoz a I sein ou li liiens chiet; puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les II seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe I poc celle moistor sus le feu; puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie; et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai I cercle, et le perce rondement entor; puis boute I fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble I dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument; et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	And it is of silver or brass, and the head is higher; and below at the groin where the ligaments fall; then take a sheep's bladder and put the moisture in which you wish to clysterize the bladder, then tie it between the two groins properly with a strong double thread, and warm that moisture over the fire; then insert the head of the clyster into the urethra, then press your hand on the bladder for all the moisture to come out gradually until the patient feels that this moisture has reached the bladder; and if you do not have the bladder, take a piece of parchment, and make a circle, and pierce it roundly around; then insert a strong thread through these holes, then close the circle as one closes a lid, and put inside what you wish of oil and moisture and water, and tie it to the instrument; and do as you did with the bladder, pressing by hand until the moisture reaches the bladder.
de la piere	of the stone
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	We have already said in the division the types of stones, and the extraction together with medicines; and I have said the difference between the stone in the kidneys, and all the signs, and in which stone one should operate by cutting; and in the bladder, and in the penis; and I will tell you clearly and briefly.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont IIII ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	I say that the stone which forms in the bladder occurs more often in children, and it is a sign that the urine jumps from the bladder resembling fine particles; and there appears sand, and it irritates the patient's penis, and it can happen many times, and then it hardens; and much of this jumping affects the foundations; and the healing is light for children until they are four years old, and it is very severe in the elderly, and it is moderate for middle-aged people, those who are between youth and old age; and the cure is lighter for those who have a large stone than for those who have a small one.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	And when we come to the treatment, it is necessary first to purify the patient with an enema, to draw out all the bile that is in the intestines.
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	For it sometimes hinders seeking the stone.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche dedens; se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere.	Then take the patient by the feet, and lift him up and move him downward so that the stone descends to the opening of the bladder, and sometimes it leaves its higher position; then make him sit between your hands arranged in this way, and his hands should be below his thighs, so that the bladder is entirely inclined downwards; then seek it and touch inside; if you feel the stone in the space, now hasten to cut into the stone.
Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	And if it does not fall at the full touch, moisten your index finger with oil from your left hand, if the patient is an adult, or your middle finger, if the patient is a fully grown young man; and insert it into his anus, and seek the stone, and when you feel it with your finger, guide it towards the neck of the bladder; then press down on your finger, and push it outwards where you wish to cut.
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille; puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	And instructs the attendant to press the bladder with his hand, and commands him to extend with his right hand the testicles upwards, and with his left hand lift the skin that is below the testicles in the area where one makes the incision; then he inserts the cutting spatula, of which this is the form:
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans; par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	And cut between what is between the testicles and the anus, not in the middle but to the side of the left thigh; and let it be straight towards the stone, and your hand should be at the anus, and let the incision be sideways so that it is wide on the outside, and narrow inside according to the size of the stone, not too large; perhaps it presses so much with the hand at the anus that it jumps out without effort; and know that there are such stones that have angles and edges: they are difficult to remove; and there are some that are beneath, resembling a grain, and round, from which the extraction is easy.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li I estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge I poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole; et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors.	To those then who have angles and margins, make the cut larger; and if it does not jump out, you must squeeze with tongs which are like a file at the head, to pull out the stone so that it does not escape; or you put under it an instrument subtle curved at the head; and if you cannot bring it out thus, then enlarge the pouch and pierce it, and if the skin is tough, thin it with vitriol; and if there are more than one stone, put the largest first into the neck of the bladder, then cut above, then pull hard, and the smaller ones after if there are many.
Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie.	And if it is very large, then it must be sawn, and make a larger incision.
Car II choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces; et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus I drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	For two things happen to the patient: either he dies, or the urine comes immediately through the opening that the skin cannot close; but nevertheless strive to pull it out, or break it with tongs, until you pull it out in pieces; and when you have completed your work, apply the wound with incense and aloe and dragon's blood, and bind it, and put over it a cloth moistened in oil and wine, or in oil and rose water and cold water, to cool the hot abscess; then raise the patient up on his back, and do not loosen the bandage until the third day.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you release it, wash the area very well with oil and water, then treat it with ointment diafinicon and basilicon ointment until it is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine: boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit; puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez; et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les II cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	And if hot abscesses and corrosions come to the wound and clots of blood in the bladder, which cause the urine to be retained in such a way that it goes out with the urine: then put your finger in the wound and extract that blood, for if it remains there, it will corrupt the bladder and destroy it; then cleanse the wound with water and ash and salt, and aid it in every way you know until it is healed; and it is necessary that every time you treat it, you bind the two thighs together and apply medicines to the area.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure.	And if the stone is small, and it is in the urethra of the penis, and stuck inside, and the urine cannot exit; then you treat it as I said before, that you cut it many times, and one is excused from the cutting by this treatment.
Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	I have already proved it thus.
Pren I foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a III angles fichiees en I tison:	Take an iron rod according to this form and let it have three pointed ends fixed in one piece.
puis pren I fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge.	then take a thread and tie it around the penis below the stone so that it cannot move back into the bladder; then insert the rod into the penis lightly until it reaches the stone; and turn the rod in your hand against the stone little by little, until you can pierce through the other side of the stone; then the urine will come out soon, then press your hand on what remains of the stone that is inside the penis.
Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides; et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie I fil desoz la piere et I autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les II liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	It is broken immediately, and passes out with the urine, and the patient is healed; and if you cannot do this for any reason that prevents it, tie a thread under the stone and another above, then cut the penis where the stone is between the two threads, then extract it forcefully, untie the thread, and clean the congealed blood in the wound; treat it until it is healed.
de la piere des femmes	of the stone of women
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por III choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	It rarely happens that a stone is formed in women, and if it ever does occur, the treatment is difficult, and it is prevented for three reasons: one is that perhaps the woman is a virgin; and the second is that one cannot find a knowledgeable woman who will expose herself to midwives, especially when she is chaste.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a. Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier I caste mire subtil; et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere; et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge: adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere; et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	And the third manner is that by chance one cannot find a woman well skilled in this art of hands; and the fourth manner is that the stone of the woman is more deep inside than the man's stone, therefore it is necessary to make a deeper cut, and there is great fear. And if necessity demands this, then you must take a midwife well skilled, and with difficulty one finds her, and if you do not find one, at least choose a subtle male doctor; and present him with a wise bailiff in the life of women, or a woman who knows part of the art, and command her to do what you order for the examination of the stone; and look well if the woman is a virgin: then she must put her finger into the fundament and seek the stone; and if she finds it, constrain it under her finger, and recommend that she put her finger into the vagina of the patient, and search and press her left hand strongly on the bladder.
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse; puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie; et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite; puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont: c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains.	If she finds it, then she must move it gradually from the entrance of the bladder down to the root of the thigh; then cut into the stone at the root of the thigh against the middle of the groin, where it is arranged for movement and feels the stone in that part; and do not move her finger above or below the stone, and let the incision be small at first; then put the probe into the incision, if you feel the stone enlarge the wound until the stone can come out easily, and know that there are many kinds of stones: to know, small and large and rough and smooth, long and round, and those that have edges.
si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	and know the similarities to understand the outcome.
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre; et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide; puis cure la plaie.	And if the pain overcomes you, then put ground vitriol at the site and keep it for an hour until the pain is subsided; then return to your work until the stone comes out, and have the instruments I told you about for extracting stones from men to help you in your work; and if the pain overcomes you, and this is from the artery that has been cut, then put the powder on the site and use bandages and wraps tightly, and do not start again with this, and leave the stone and do not treat it, so that by chance the patient might not die; then heal the wound.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	And when the heat of the blood is calmed, and the flesh softens, then return to your work, until the stone is removed.
de hernie carnouse	of a fleshy hernia
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit I autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	Aqueous ramice is nothing other than a collection of moisture or white syfac, which is beneath the shell of the testicles that contain the egg; and it is called "syfac," and sometimes it properly adheres to the membrane of the egg, so that one might think it is another egg; and this is the skin of the testicle between the white syfac that we have mentioned; and this does not happen often.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the generation of this ramice is due to weakness that affects the testicles, and that material is spread out.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus; et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, I poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	And sometimes it comes from a blow to the testicles, and this moisture has many colors: or it is a color leaning towards yellow, or without red, or black, or white watery, and this happens more; and these are the signs to recognize this assembly, for if it is as white as we have said, then the abscess is hard, about as long as the shape of an egg, and the testicles do not appear, because they are surrounded by moisture.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef; et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien; donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	And if there is moisture in the inner membrane, then the abscess is hard like part of an egg, and for this reason it is thought to be another egg; and if the moisture is between the skin of the testicles and the white as described, one can feel it well; therefore when you want to know the color of the moisture, examine all around the introitus, from which the form is mentioned above.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	According to what comes after the introduction, judge of what is within.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors; puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz; puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des II costelz dou keur des coions; puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir; puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a I large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont; et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement; cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue; et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac; puis assemble les II leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when we treat it with iron, the patient must be bled according to our ability and the fullness of his body; then he is placed on his back, on something slightly raised, and put under him many cloths; then sit on his left side, and instruct the assistant to sit on the right, and extend the rod to one of the two sides of the testicles' core; then take the spatula and cut the skin of the testicles down the middle from the long part up to near the tip, and let that cut be straight through dividing the skin of the testicles all the way to the white surface, and scrape it delicately according to our ability; then pierce the white surface full of fluid with a wide hole, and drain all the fluid, and then place your probes, and stretch the white surface upwards; do not touch the core of the testicles but only the white surface; cut everything entirely or in pieces carefully on its side as well, for if you do not cut it properly, the fluid will return; and if the egg jumps during your work, reset it in place when you have completed the work on the white surface; then stitch together the two ends of the testicles' core with a seam, then treat it like other wounds until it is healed.
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc; puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	And if you find the egg corrupted by another disease, then it is necessary that you tie the vessels which are suspensory, fearing the flow of blood; then cut off the testicle with all its suspensory ligament, and extract the egg, and cure it as we have said.
Et se aigue est assemblee en II parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont II ramices; si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset; et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les II coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	And if the fluid is collected in two parts together, know that these are two branches; then cut off the other part as you have done the first equally, then wipe the blood, and put in the wound wool moistened with rose oil; and place another layer of wool moistened with wine and oil, and put it on both testicles, and put over them doubled cloths, and bind it all with a bandage according to this form:
Puis pren II drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil; et li autre dui chief sus les II angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier; et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes I cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers; si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	Then take two cloths, and fill them with shredded wool according to this pattern and let them be sewn together at the waistband of the breeches, and one of the shoulders should reach from the anus to the back, and the other to the part of the groin; and the other two ends on the two sides, and let all be gathered in the loop of the breechcloth; and sometimes this branch is treated with cautery instead of iron scissors, and it is that you take a subtle knife-shaped cautery, and cut the skin of the testicles, and heat it as we have said, so that the white surface containing the fluid is exposed; then take the cautery according to this form, and pierce that surface with the points, and scrape it with this heated subtle cautery:
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout; et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef; et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve; et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille; et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	And cut in all ways that you can, until you scrape everything clean; and be careful that the fire does not touch the eye; and know that this work is more secure; and watch for any bleeding, and make smaller what you carve; and if anything opposes you, whether an abscess or bleeding or something else, then treat whatever opposes you as was previously said.
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai, si fai seoir le malaide sus I siege leveit; pues perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors; et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer; puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee; et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant; et eslarge I poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés VI mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	And if the patient is fearful and does not want to undergo this work due to its horror, use perforation as I tell you; and know that when you are certain by the signs we have mentioned that water branch is there, make the patient sit on a raised seat; then pierce the abscess at the part below all the thickness wide, and place the perforation of the long body; let the holes be wide so that all the water flows out freely; then put cotton on the spot, tie it up, and leave it to drain the remaining water; then treat until the wound is healed; and if the white cloth does not allow water to come out from the mouth of the wound, you must pierce with a quill or the instrument used to draw water from dropsical people, whose form is as previously described; enlarge the spot of the wound, and know that the water returns and collects after six months or around there, and when it has collected again as before, thus will the patient spend his days.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess of the testicles
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse; et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	Know that in the section of this branch there is fear in many positions, which is why it seems better to leave it alone; and I will tell you the work and the similarities of the abscess.
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions; et c’est par mout de cas.	I say then that many abscesses come to the body, and especially to the testicles; and this is by much chance.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion; et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors; et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief; et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	It is to know by excess of sour and watery substances, which spreads to the testicles, or from percussion; and the color of the abscess is according to the color of the body; and there is no pain found, and it is a severe abscess; and by chance some severe abscesses are fearful and stony, and of flushed color, and sometimes comes from a knot in an artery, or swelling of a vein.
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois; et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	When it is by artery, it is known by the arrangement of hot abscess, when you press it with your fingers; and you should not touch it.
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois, et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars; et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	He who is affected by vein swelling is known by its appearance upon touching with the fingers, and one can properly perform the incision on this likeness, and on other forms; and it is that you cut the core of the testicles, then the egg rises, and the string comes out from the white part, and release the suspensory ligament from all around the egg.
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope; et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	If the egg is already swollen with these new forms, then you must draw out the egg and cut it; and if it is airy on the surface or inside the vessels, you must release all of that tension and cut it roundly.
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	And if the birth of the flesh is at the back place, then you must cut it all away and extract the egg, just as we have said.
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when your work is completed, apply the wound with wool soaked in rose oil and wine, then treat it with other treatments until it is healed.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess of the testicles
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a I borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions, et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait; et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant, et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	This is an abscess wrapped in a wrapping similar to a boil, with the swelling of the testicles, and the patient suffers greatly when urinating; and the treatment of this disease is as fearful as the one mentioned before, yet we will still tell you the procedure for it, according to what the ancients did.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois, a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment; puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert, et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples; puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait I fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief; puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues; puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions; car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz; si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	You should make the patient sit on an elevated chair, then put the suspensory of the testicles down to your hands, at all the vessels that are close to the penis, and hold them firmly, and stretch them well; then cut with a sharp broad blade from across the vessels until they are uncovered, and then peel off each side as we have said in the extraction of arteries which are in temples; then stick a needle where it has double thread, and tie it at the first place where the seed comes out, and tie it again at the other end; then cut straight through the middle according to the length of the body, and draw out the corrupt moisture; then treat the wound as with others where you apply ointment, so that no vessel falls which nourishes one of the testicles; because by this there comes no harm, and if all the vessels come to seed, it is necessary to draw the testicles at all the vessels; so that the semen does not lose its nourishment due to the cutting of the vessels, they dry out and cannot heal.
de la routure dou syfac	of the rupture of the thigh
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions; et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces II manieres de mout de causes: ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses; et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement; et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	The occurrences of this rupture are by the section that affects the thigh, or by extension on the belly in the area of the ankles, causing the intestines to descend from that rupture into one of the testicles; and this rupture is either in the thigh itself, or in its extension, and these two types come from causes: by impact, or jumping, or straining, or lifting heavy loads, and by similar things; and the signs when it is an extension of the thigh are that it happens gradually over a long time, not suddenly; and the swelling is gradual until perfect, because the thigh compresses the intestines.
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.	And the sign is when it is of the section of the thigh, that it brings sudden pain at the beginning, and the swelling appears different beneath the skin near, and this is due to the protrusion of the intestines and the body beyond the thigh.
Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez.	And sometimes the hernias descend with the intestines, and are retained there, causing great pain to the patient, especially when they are pressed.
Et en ces cures de fer a paor, por coi il s’en covient eschuir.	And in these iron treatments there is fear, therefore one must avoid them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que tu comande ou malaide qu’il ramoine l’intestine a sa main au dedens en la plaie, s’il i puet rentreir; puis soit sovinez sus son col. entre tes mains, et lieve les cuixes; puis estent le keur au desus, et cope tout le cuir des coions dou lonc; puis boute dedens les leivres de la taille uncines selonc ceu que tu en as mestier por ovrir la plaie, et soit telz que li oes em puist issir; puis escorche lou syfac que est desoz lou cuir des coions, tant que li blans syfac dur soit descovers de toutes pars; puis boute ton doi indice en ceu qui enseut lou coion, en ceu qui est entre lou blanc syfac qui est desoz lou cuir de l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac, et depart ceu qui est derrier l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac; et pues muef a la main destre dedens lou keur des coions, et estent lou blanc syfac en haut a ta main senestre, et lieve l’uef a tout lou syfac devers la taille; et comande au ministre qu’il estende l’uef en haut, et deslie ceu qui est aers derrier le liement; et quier a tes dois s’il a point de l’intestine envoloupeit ou blanc syfac dur, et se tu en trueves aucune chose, si le boute au ventre desoz; puis pren une aguille ou il ait I gros fil fait de X filz, et la boute en la derriere partie dou syfac, qui est aprés lou cuir des coions; aprés la taille, puis cope les chiés qui apperent des filz, tant qu’il i ait IIII filz; puis les assemble l’un sus l’autre en maniere de croix, et en lie lou syfac, dont nos avons dit qui est desoz lou cuir des coions, d’un fort liien de II pars;
