And in the case where the dislocation is fresh, and it is one of the four types of dislocations, you must hurry to return the joint, stretch it inside and outside, and move it left and right; perhaps it will return, and no other treatment is needed.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles I ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a II mains, ou a I liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil; et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe; et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien; et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	And if it does not return in this manner, you must prepare one assistant to strongly stretch the leg with both hands, or by tying a rope above the knee; and another assistant extends his hand over in such a way that he places his hands under the bones, then tightly binds them with a strong rope on the thigh; and another holds the end of the rope; and they pull up and down all at once so that the patient is lifted from the ground at once, and remains hanging.
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as IIII semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This method of extension is common to the four similar cases, and if the dislocation has returned, as we have said, it is good.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele; puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment: si revenra a son leu maintenant; et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	If not, then it is necessary to attend to its similarity. When the dislocation is at the outer side, you must place the patient on his healthy side, then put the bandage on the root of the thigh and the spot below the angle, then extend the bandage upward toward the angle and toward the force; then have another minister take his arms, and grasp the large part of the diseased thigh, and stretch it upwards strongly: it will return to its place now; and this type of dislocation is lighter than the others.
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les II piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les II talons, et sus les II genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue II dois plus que li autres; puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre II bras de lonc; puis comande a I ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	And if you cannot secure it in the manner we have said, then you must bind the two feet of the patient together with a strong bond above both heels and both knees, and let the diseased leg be stretched out two times more than the other; then hang him from the head of a post, and let him be two arms' length off the ground; then command one minister to grasp the top of the thigh, and have another minister hanging with the patient, who firmly holds the thigh, for the joint returns very quickly now.
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne I liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi; puis met II tisons, I au chief et I autre as piez, puis fiche I tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme; et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	And when the dislocation is on the foot, the patient lies down as we have said in that which has gilbositeit, and binds the joint properly on the sick leg and also on the thigh; then puts two sticks, one at the head and another at the feet, then places one stick between the legs of the patient in the shape; and has planted around with wet cloths so it does not hurt the patient, then stretches each minister towards him, and the doctor places equally with his hand the dislocation.
S’elle revient, c’est boin.	If it returns, it is good.
Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	If not, put it on a table, and press it as we have said in the case of gilbositeit, and lay the patient on the healthy side.
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit; et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	And when the dislocation is in front, it is necessary to stretch the diseased leg quickly, and according to what I have said; and let the physician put his force on the sick joint, then press with the other hand, and extend downwards towards the knee.
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les II hainches; et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table; et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz; adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve; et se repose III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus; et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse III jors; puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And if the dislocation is at the back, it is not necessary to stretch the patient downwards or lift them up from the ground, but they should be as if their hip was dislocated at the back, just as we have said about lying on both hips; and let them lie on their face, and the limb extended as we have said before, and one must press on the joint with a board; it will be correct when the patient stretches his legs, and they are equal; then align the thighs, apply the poultice, and bind with a bandage so that the hip does not move; and let them rest for three or four days, then unbind them, and apply another poultice on top; and if you see that they are equal, then bind again as before, and leave it for three days; then unbind, and make him walk gently until the limb is strengthened.
de la dislocation dou genoil	of the dislocation of the knee
Li genous est desaluez selonc III manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	The knee is dislocated in three ways: to be known, inward and outward, and backward; and it does not dislocate forward.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez; et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez; puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les II costez dou genoil forment; et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement; et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie; et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And the sign is that you instruct the patient to bend his leg at the thigh, and if it does not straighten at the thigh, know that it is dislocated; and the restoration of all such cases is that you make the patient sit upright, and extend his leg if he can, and place your back on his chest, and put his foot on your feet; then take his knee in your palms, and pull between your hands, then bend both sides of the knee firmly; another assistant extends his foot until the knee returns to its place, and the sign is that it straightens well at the thigh lightly; and apply the plaster, and make the leg adhere to the thigh, and bind them together tightly for three or four days, then untie it; and let the patient not exert himself in walking until the limb is strengthened.
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez	And if the limb is not completely healed, apply strong extension, as we have said in the treatment of the hip, until it is healed.
de la dislocation dou talon	of the dislocation of the heel
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The heel is sometimes displaced, and sometimes completely dislocated, inside and out.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee: li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	And the signs are that the ankle is swollen, and extends forward where it is dislocated: the resetting is light, and it should be gently stretched by hand when it is only displaced.
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville; puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut; et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet; s’elle revient, c’est bien; se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient; et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide; puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet; puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent; puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	And when it is completely dislocated, you should make the patient sit upright, and have one assistant firmly hold the leg above the ankle; then pull the foot towards you with your right hand, and then with your left hand two times, then stretch it upwards, and gently push the foot upwards; do this two times as we have said, by pushing and pulling the foot; if it returns, that is good; if not, repeat the procedure, for it will return; and if it cannot be returned in this way, make the patient lie on his back on the ground, and firmly place a stick between his thighs, and wrap cloth around it so as not to injure the patient; then have one assistant hold the thigh, and another assistant stretch the foot with their hands or using a rope tied above the ankle; then each assistant should stretch equally, and the stick should be between the patient's thighs to hold the patient in place when stretching; then the physician places his hands equally on the dislocation, and another assistant holds the healthy leg below, and the dislocation will return quickly.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois; puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain; puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors; et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	And when it is at the right point, put the plaster and bandages on, bind firmly, tie the foot to the leg, and watch the nerves that are above the ankle behind, so the binding is not too tight; then leave for two days or three, and if the binding loosens, rebind; then untie on the third day or fourth, and forbid walking for four days; and if he walks before this term, it is not certain that it will not dislocate again.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if hot abscesses come, you must soothe them, as we have said elsewhere, until they are healed.
des dois	of the two
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When both are dislocated, they must be gently extended without effort, and this is an easy thing to do.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne; et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the dislocation is in any joint of the back of the foot, then you must make the patient sit on a flat place or on a table completely straight, and put your foot on what appears of his joints, then press strongly with your foot until it returns; and when it is aligned and nothing protrudes, then put under the sole of the foot a board at two angles, then pull strongly, and leave for three days, then loosen it; and make him rest until he is healed.
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	of wound and dislocation together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert: si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis; et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit; et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne; et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis; et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples; et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	When a wound comes with the dislocation and you wish to restore it, often the patient dies: so be not presumptuous in the treatment if you are not skilled in the art and have not practiced long, and if you are not compassionate and merciful and cautious, not bold; and use at the beginning things that calm hot abscesses, and leave the patient in God's hands if you see no hope of health; and when you see hope, then reset now the limb to its place, as soon as the hot abscess comes; and when the limb is in place, then administer things that calm hot abscesses, and treat the wound as it should be with drying ointments; and if there is a break with the dislocation and small bones are detached, remove them, and do what we have said in simple diseases; and beware of entering a path of fear according to what I have said, for this does not suit you according to your Creator, and for the wisdom of your arm and body.
Amen	Amen
